وہ بمعنى المستقبل ہے ۔ ولا تقول ايتنی اکرمتك یہ مثال غلط ہے کیونکہ یہاں امر ہے اور کے جواب میں کلمہ ان مقدر ہو گا۔ اصل یوں ہے اتنی ان ایتتنی اگر متک تو میہاں ان مقدر ہے لہذا یہ ماضی کو بمعنی مستقبل نہیں کر سکتا بل يجب بلکہ واجب ہے کہ جواب امر میں مضارع استعمال کریں اور کہیں اتنی اکر ملک - وکذا فی الجملة الاسميه اور یہی حال جملہ اسمیہ میں رہے گا کہ ان ملفوظ کی صورت میں بمعنی مستقبل ہوگا جواب درست ہو گا اور یوں کہہ سکتے ہیں ان تاتنی مانت مکرم ولا تقول انتنی فانت مکرم کیونکہ جواب امر میں ان مقدر ہے جو بمعنی مستقبل نہیں کریگا لہذا جواب صحیح نہیں ہوگا فكما لا تجعل ان المقدرة جیسے ان مقدرہ ماضی کو بمعنی مستقبل نہیں کر سکتا اسی طرح جملہ اسمیہ کو بھی بمعنی مستقبل نہیں کر سکتا بل اد کی بلکہ بطریق اولی جملہ اسمیہ کو بمعنی مستقبل نہیں کرے گا۔ لان مدلول الجملة الاسمية کیونکہ جملہ اسمیہ کا مدلول بعید از مستقبل ہے اور ماضی کمدلول قریب الی المستقبل ہے لاشتراكهما یعنی ماضی اور مستقبل دونوں فعل ہونے میں اور دلالت علی الزمان میں مشترک ہیں فلما لم تجعل تو جب ان مقدرہ ماضی کو بمعنی مستقبل نہیں کر سکتا تو جملہ اسمیہ کو بمعنی مستقبل بطریق اولی نہیں کر سکے گا لہذا جملہ اسمیہ جواب امر نہیں ہو سکتا تو فانت حراز کا جواب نہیں ہے اور نہ از پر مرتب ہے لہذا غلام ازاد ہو جائے گا خواہ الف ادا کرے یا نہ کر۔
It [the particle] has the meaning of future. And do not say 'taeni akramtuka' [come to me I honored you]; this example is wrong because here there is a command and in its answer the word 'in' is implied. The original is: 'taeni in atitani' [come to me if you come to me] – if you speak then here 'in' is implied, therefore this cannot make the past into the future. Rather it is obligatory to use the present tense in the answer to the command. And similarly in the nominal sentence, the same applies: if 'in' is explicit, it will have the meaning of future and the answer will be correct, so you can say 'in tatini ana akramuka' [if you come to me I will honor you]. And do not say 'tatini fa-anta mukramun' [you come to me so you are honored] because in the answer to the command 'in' is implied, which will not make it future. Therefore the answer is not correct. Just as the implied 'in' cannot make the past into the future, similarly it cannot make the nominal sentence into the future. Rather, by primary analogy, the nominal sentence will not make the future, because the denotation of the nominal sentence is far from the future while the denotation of the past is close to the future due to their shared characteristic – that both past and future are verbs and share in indication of time. So when the implied 'in' cannot make the past into the future, then it cannot make the nominal sentence into the future by primary analogy. Therefore the nominal sentence cannot be the answer to the command. Thus 'fa-anta hurrun' [so you are free] is not an answer and not connected to the command, so the slave will be freed whether he pays the alif or not.
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the grammatical rule that the conditional particle 'in' when implicit does not convert a past tense verb to future meaning. The author explains that in the answer to an imperative, an implicit 'in' is assumed, so the verb must be present or future, not past. For example, saying 'taeni akramtuka' (come to me, I honored you) is incorrect. The correct form is to use the present tense, e.g., 'taeni akramuka'. The same applies to nominal sentences: if 'in' is explicit (like 'in tatini ana akramuka'), the nominal sentence is fine, but if 'in' is implied, the nominal sentence cannot serve as the answer. The reasoning is that nominal sentences denote a state far from the future, while past tense verbs are closer to the future because both are verbs. Therefore, by analogy (qiyas), if the implied 'in' cannot make a past verb future, it is even less able to make a nominal sentence future. The passage concludes with an example: if someone says 'taeni fa-anta hurrun' (come to me, so you are free), the slave is freed immediately, whether he pays the alif (a sum of money) or not.

Key Terms
ان (in): The conditional particle meaning 'if', used in classical Arabic to introduce a conditional clause.
ان مقدرة (in muqaddara): An implicit or understood 'in' that is not pronounced but is grammatically assumed.
جملة اسمية (jumla ismiyya): A nominal sentence (beginning with a noun or pronoun), used to describe a state or permanent attribute.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the correct answer to the imperative 'taeni' (come to me)?
A) 'taeni akramtuka' (come to me, I honored you)
B) 'taeni akramuka' (come to me, I honor you)
C) 'in tatini akramuka' (if you come to me, I honor you)
D) 'taeni fa-anta mukramun' (come to me, so you are honored)

Key Takeaway
Explicit 'in' converts past to future; implicit 'in' does not, and by qiyas it cannot convert nominal sentences either.

The Legal Function of 'Lakin' as Istidrak
Explains the particle 'lakin' as istidrak with condition of coherence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when 'lakin' functions as istidrak and apply the condition of coherence to determine whether both parts of the statement are established or the latter part is a new independent statement.

Core Idea
Lakin corrects the prior statement only if coherent and the latter can rectify the former.

In Hanafi legal reasoning, particles like 'lakin' carry significant weight. Understanding whether 'lakin' introduces a correction (istidrak) or an entirely new statement determines how a legal admission, testimony, or ruling is interpreted. This lesson unpacks the rule from the text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the particle 'lakin'
Locate 'lakin' in the legal statement. It is the key word that triggers the analysis.
2
Examine the connection between the two parts
Determine if the speech is coherent (mustaqim) and if what follows 'lakin' is related to and can rectify what precedes.
Coherence implies logical connection, not just grammatical.
3
Apply the rule
If coherent and rectification is possible, then both the negation and affirmation are established together; otherwise, the part after 'lakin' is a new independent statement.
This distinction affects legal outcomes.
4
Test with examples
Use the house case: Bakr's statement 'it was never mine but it is Zaid's' is coherent, so both parts take effect.
This leads to Bakr's liability.

میں ثابت ہو جائے پھر ثانیا بعض کا اخراج کیا جائے بلکہ دونوں معا ثابت ہیں بیک وقت ان کا ثبوت ہوگا۔ وعلى هذا قالوا في المقضى له بدار بالبينة یعنی اس بنا پر کہ بیان تغیر میں صدر کلام موقوف على الآخر ہوتا ہے اور اول و آخر دونوں کا حکم معا ثابت ہوتا ہے تو فقہا نے کہا مقتضی لہ بدار میں صورت اس کی یہ ہے کہ دار کمرو کے قبضہ میں تھی تو بکر نے اس کے خلاف دعومٹی کیا کہ یہ دار میری ہے ۔ عمرو نے اس کا انکار کر دیا تو بکر نے اپنے دعوئی پر بینہ یعنی شاہد قائم کر دیئے قاضی نے دار کا فیصلہ بحق بکر کر دیا یہی بکر ہے مقصنی کہ بدار بالبيزه او قال ما كانت لی قط لكنها الزید نہیں بکر جو مقعی کہ بدار ہے وہ بعد القضاء کہتا ہے کہ یہ دار میری کبھی نہیں تھی لیکن یہ وار زید کی ہے و قال زید باع منی الخ تو زید اس اقرار کی جو کہ بکر نے کہا ہے کہ یہ دار زید کی ہے تصدیق کرتا ہے اور بکر نے جو کہا کہ ما کانت لی قط اس کی تکذیب کرتا ہے اور وہ یہ کہتا ہے کہ بعد القضاً اس نے میرے پاس فروخت کی ہے یاوہ کہتا ہے کہ اس نے مجھے صبر کی ہے یہی مراد ہے باغ منی اور صب لی بعد القضاء ان الدار الزید اس صورت میں دار تو زید کی ہوگی وعلی المقضی نام اور قاضی نے جس کے حق میں قضا بالبینہ کی تھی یعنی بکو پر اس دار کی قیمت واجب ہوگی للمتقضی علیہ یہ اس کو ادا کرے گا جس کے خلاف فیصلہ ہوا ہے یعنی عمرو کو لانه اذا وصل کیونکہ جب لکنہا کو اس نے متصلا بولا تو گویا کہ نفی اور استدراک بلکن اس نے معا بولا ہے فیثبت موجبهما معاً تو دونوں کا مقتضا معاً ثابت ہو جائے گا یعنی اپنے نفس کے لئے نفی ملک اور ثبوت ملک برائے زید ۔ ثم تكذيب الشعور اب اس کا لازمی نتیجہ یہ ہے کہ جن شہود نے اس بکر کے حق میں شہادت دی تھی ان کی تکذیب ہوگی اور ملک کا اثبات برائے مقضی علیہ یعنی عمر د کے لئے ہوگا اور یہ دونوں کلاموں کے یعنی نفی عن نفسہ اور ثبوت ملک برائے زید کے بعد ثابت ہوگا - فيكون حجة یہ صرف مقضى له یعنی بکر کے خلاف تو یہ حجت ہوگا زید کے خلاف حجت نہیں ہو سکتا کیونکہ یہ اقرارہ علی نفسہ ہے جو حجت قاصرہ ہے لہذا دار زید کی ہوگی اور عمرو کو ضمان قیمت ادا کرے گا ۔ تم ان انستق الکلام یہ بحث اول یعنی یہ کہ لکن برائے استدراک ہے اس کی طرف رجوع ہے یعنی اگر کلام متسق ہو اور لکن کا ما بعد ماقبل کے ساتھ متعلق اور مرتبط ہو اى يصلح ان يكون ارتباط سے مراد یہ ہے ماقبل کے لئے لکن کا مابعد تدارک ہونے کی صلاحیت رکھتا ہو تو اسے تدارک پر محمول کیا جائے گا والا اگر اتساق اور ارتباط در میان ماقبل و ما بعد کے نہ ہو اور لکن کا ما بعد صلاحیت استدراک نہ رکھتے تو پھر نہر کلا در مستانف تو ما بعد کو کلام مستانف قرار دیا جائیگا نحولك على الف قرض یہ نظیر اتساق ہے یعنی ایک شخص اقرار کرتا ہے کہ تیرا میرے اوپر الف بطور قرض کے ہے۔ فقال المقوله مقزلہ کہتا لا مکن غصب یعنی قرض تو نہیں لیکن غصب ہے تو یہ کلام متسق ہے

تو وصل صحیح ہو گا نفی سبب ہو گی نفی واجب نہیں ہوگی ۔ فان قوله لا لا یمکن الخز یعنی لفظ لا کوننی واجب پر محمول کرنا ممکن نہیں لانه لو حمل یعنی اگر اس کو نفی واجب پر محمول کریں یعنی مقرلہ کی مراد یہ ہو کہ الف تیرے ذمہ واجب نہیں ہے تو پھر اگل قول لکن غصب کا بولنا مستقیم اور صحیح نہیں ہو سکتا کیونکہ جب الف سرے سے واجب ہی نہیں تو پھر اس کے واجب ہونے کی کوئی صورت نہیں ہو سکتی لہذا لکن غصب غلط ہو جائیگا پھر کلام متسق نہیں ہو سکتی لہذا الفظ لا نفی سبب ہے نفی واجب نہیں ۔ مقصد یہ ہے کہ بطور قرض نہیں پھر اس کا تدارک کیا یہ تو نے غصب کیا تھا تو اس صورت میں کلام مرتبط ہو جائے گی فلا يكون رداً لا قرارة. یہ رد اقرار نہیں ہوگا بلکہ صرف نفی سبب ہوگی۔ بخلاف ما اذا تزوجت الامة بغير ازن مولدها به غر منسق کی مثال ہے جہاں ما بعد لکن تدارک ماقبل کی صلاحیت نہیں رکھتا وہ یہ کہ ایک مملوکہ بغیر ازن مولیٰ کے یکصد حق المصر کے عوض کسی کے ساتھ نکاح کر لیتی ہے جب مولی کو اطلاع ہوتی ہے تو وہ کہتا ہے لا اجيز النکاح میں اس نکاح کو جائز قرار نہیں دیتا لیکن اجیزه بمائتین لیکن میں اس کو دوصد کے ساتھ جائزہ قرار دیتا ہوں تو اس صورت میں منفسخ النکاح جو نکاح اس لونڈی نے کیا تھا وہ فسخ ہو جائیت کا عن اصلہ یعنی لا اجیز النکاح کے ساتھ اصل نکاح فسخ ہو جا سگا وجعل لكن مبتداء اور لیکن سے کلام مخالف ہو گی جو کہ ماقبل کے ساتھ مرتبط نہیں ہو سکتی لانه لا يمكن اثبات هذا النکاح بمائتیین یعنی اسی نکاح کا جو اصلا فسخ ہو چکا ہے تو اب اجیزہ بمائتین کے ساتھ اس نکاح کا جو عن اصلہ فسخ ہو چکا ہے اثبات بمائتین ممکن نہیں ہے تو اس مسئلہ میں کلام متسق و مربوط نہ رہی ما بعد تدارک ماقبل نہیں ہو سکتا لان الساقة کیوں کہ اس کا اتساق مقتضی ہے کہ ان لا يصح النكاح الأول یعنی جو نکاح اول ہو چکا ہے وہ سرے صحیح نہ رہے لیکن مانتیں کے ساتھ پھر صحیح ہو جائے ڈالا یمکن اور یہ ناممکن ہے لانہ کیونکہ جب اس مولیٰ نے کہا لا اجيز النکاح تو نکاح اول تو سرے سے فسخ ہو جائیگا۔ پھر اس مفسوخ نکاح کا اثبات بمائتین ممکن نہیں ہے۔ فيكون نفى ذلك النکاح کیونکہ ایک ہی نکاح کی نفی پھر بعینہ اسی کا اثبات ہو یہ نہیں ہو سکتا فعلم تو معلوم ہوا کہ یہ کلام غیر مشتق ہے لہذا لیکن اجیزہ بمائتین کو کلام مستانف قرار دیا جائے گا۔ یہ دوسرے نکاح کی اجازت ہوگی جس کی مھر مائتین ہو۔ البتہ قاضی خاں میں ہے کہ اگر یوں کہے کہ لا اجیزہ ہمانہ لکن اجیہانتیں تو پھر اصل نکاح فسخ نہیں ہوگا بلکہ یہ صرف مقدار مصر میں تدارک ہوگا ۔
(Then it is established, then secondly some part is excluded, rather both are established together. And based on this they said regarding the one judged in favor of regarding a house by evidence: meaning, on the basis that in the expression of change, the first part of speech is dependent on the latter, and both the first and last are ruled together. So the jurists said: the case of the one judged in favor of regarding a house is that the house was in the possession of Amr, then Bakr brought a claim against him saying 'this house is mine'. Amr denied it, so Bakr established evidence, i.e., witnesses, for his claim. The judge decided the house in favor of Bakr. This is Bakr, the one judged in favor of. Then Bakr says after the judgment: 'This house was never mine, but it is Zaid's'. And Zaid confirms Bakr's statement that the house is Zaid's, but denies Bakr's statement 'it was never mine' and says 'he sold it to me after the judgment' or 'he gifted it to me'. This is meant by 'sold to me' and 'gifted to me after the judgment that the house is for Zaid'. In this case, the house will be Zaid's, and the one judged in favor of, i.e., Bakr, will owe the value of the house to the one judged against, i.e., Amr. Because when he uttered 'lakinnaha' (but it is) contiguously, it is as if he uttered negation and correction together, so both their implications are established together, i.e., denial of ownership for himself and affirmation of ownership for Zaid. Then the necessary consequence is that the witnesses who testified for Bakr are discredited, and ownership is established for the one judged against, i.e., Amr. And this will be established after both statements: denial of self and affirmation of ownership for Zaid. So it is a proof; it will be a proof only against the one judged in favor of, i.e., Bakr, not against Zaid, because this is an admission against himself, which is a limited proof. Therefore, the house will be Zaid's and he will pay the guarantee of price to Amr. Then, the discussion returns to the first point, i.e., that 'lakin' is for correction. Meaning, if the speech is coherent and what follows 'lakin' is related and connected to what precedes, i.e., it is suitable to be a rectification, then it is interpreted as rectification. But if there is no coherence and connection between what precedes and what follows, and what follows 'lakin' does not have the potential for rectification, then it is treated as an independent statement. An example of coherence is: a person admits 'You have one thousand over me as a loan.' Then he says 'No, it is usurpation.' This speech is coherent. So it is correct that it is negation of cause, not negation of obligation. Because his saying 'la' cannot be interpreted as negation of obligation, because if it were interpreted as negation of obligation, i.e., 'the thousand is not obligatory upon me', then the subsequent word 'but usurpation' cannot be correct, because when the thousand is not obligatory at all, there is no way for it to be obligatory, so 'but usurpation' would be wrong and the speech would not be coherent. Therefore, the word 'la' is negation of cause, not negation of obligation. The point is that it is not as a loan, then he rectified by saying you had usurped it. In this case, the speech becomes connected, so it is not a rejection of the admission; rather it is only a negation of cause. Contrast this with the case where a slave girl marries without her master's permission for a dower of one hundred. When the master is informed, he says 'I do not permit the marriage, but I permit it with two hundred.' In this case, the marriage is annulled from its foundation, i.e., with 'I do not permit the marriage' the original marriage is annulled, and the 'but' starts a new statement that is not connected to what precedes, because it is impossible to establish this marriage with two hundred, i.e., this marriage which has already been annulled from its foundation, establishing it with two hundred is impossible. So in this issue, the speech is not coherent and connected; what follows cannot rectify what precedes, because coherence requires that the first marriage not be valid, but then become valid with two hundred, which is impossible. Because when the master said 'I do not permit the marriage', the first marriage is annulled altogether. Then establishing the annulled marriage with two hundred is impossible. Thus, this speech is not coherent. Therefore, 'but I permit it with two hundred' is treated as an independent statement; it is a permission for another marriage with a dower of two hundred. However, in Qadi Khan it is mentioned that if he says 'I do not permit this marriage, but I permit it with two hundred', then the original marriage is not annulled; rather, this is only a rectification in the amount of the dower.)
Source pages p. 349

Commentary
This passage is a usul rule explaining the particle 'lakin' (but) and its legal effect when used for istidrak (correction). The author begins by establishing that when 'lakin' is used contiguously (muttasil) with the preceding statement, both parts—the negation and the affirmation—are established simultaneously. He provides the case of a house dispute: Bakr wins a judgment based on evidence, but then says 'it was never mine, but it is Zaid's.' Because 'lakin' connects the two statements, Bakr's denial of ownership for himself and his affirmation of Zaid's ownership both take effect. Consequently, the house goes to Zaid, but Bakr must pay its value to Amr (the original possessor) because Bakr's admission against himself is a limited proof. The author then revisits the rule: 'lakin' is interpreted as istidrak only if the speech is coherent (mustaqim) and the latter part can rectify (tadaruk) the former. If the speech lacks coherence, the part after 'lakin' is treated as a new independent statement. Two examples illustrate this: coherent case—a person says 'you have 1000 as a loan' then 'no, it is usurpation.' Here 'no' negates the cause (loan), not the obligation, so the speech is coherent and the admission stands with the correction. Incoherent case—a master says 'I do not permit the marriage, but I permit it with 200.' The first part annuls the marriage, so the second cannot rectify it; thus, it becomes a new offer for a different marriage. An exception from Qadi Khan: if the master explicitly says 'I do not permit this marriage, but I permit it with 200,' the original marriage is not annulled; instead, the 'but' serves to rectify the dower amount only. This nuanced discussion demonstrates the Hanafi method of analyzing linguistic particles in legal contexts.

Key Terms
لکن (lakin): A particle indicating istidrak (correction) when the speech is coherent and the latter part can rectify the former.
استدراك (istidrak): Rectification or correction of a preceding statement by a subsequent one connected via 'lakin'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What condition must be met for 'lakin' to function as istidrak?
A) The speech must be in Arabic.
B) The speech must be coherent and the latter part must have the potential to rectify the former.
C) The 'lakin' must be immediately after the first statement.
D) The speaker must intend correction.

Key Takeaway
Lakin functions as istidrak only when the speech is coherent and the subsequent part can rectify the preceding one; otherwise, it starts a new independent statement.

Applying the Rule of 'Lakin': Examples from Legal Cases
Provides application examples of the 'lakin' rule

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the condition of coherence of 'lakin' to new legal scenarios and distinguish between coherent and incoherent uses, including the Qadi Khan exception.

Core Idea
The coherence condition determines whether a statement with 'lakin' corrects the prior or starts anew.

Building on the rule of 'lakin' as istidrak, this lesson walks through the two key examples from the text: the loan case (coherent) and the marriage permission case (incoherent). The Qadi Khan exception shows that even the marriage case can be interpreted as rectification if the wording explicitly references the same marriage.

Guided Path
1
Recall the rule
Remember: 'lakin' is istidrak only if speech is coherent and latter part can rectify former.
2
Analyze the loan example
Person admits debt as loan, then says 'No, it is usurpation.' The 'no' negates the cause (loan), not the obligation. The speech is coherent because the second part corrects the description of the debt.
Result: both statements are effective; debt is admitted as usurpation.
3
Analyze the marriage example
Master says 'I do not permit the marriage, but I permit it with 200.' The first part annuls the marriage; the second cannot rectify a void marriage. So incoherent; the second part is a new independent statement (offer for a new marriage).
Result: first marriage annulled, second statement is permission for a different marriage.
4
Understand the Qadi Khan exception
If the master says 'I do not permit this marriage, but I permit it with 200,' then the 'but' can rectify the dower amount only, without annulling the marriage. This requires explicit reference to 'this marriage'.
Exception shows nuance: the wording 'this marriage' signals intent to rectify the dower, not annul.
5
Apply to new scenarios
Test your understanding by evaluating if a given 'lakin' statement is coherent or not.
Practice with the tasks.

تو وصل صحیح ہو گا نفی سبب ہو گی نفی واجب نہیں ہوگی ۔ فان قوله لا لا یمکن الخز یعنی لفظ لا کوننی واجب پر محمول کرنا ممکن نہیں لانه لو حمل یعنی اگر اس کو نفی واجب پر محمول کریں یعنی مقرلہ کی مراد یہ ہو کہ الف تیرے ذمہ واجب نہیں ہے تو پھر اگل قول لکن غصب کا بولنا مستقیم اور صحیح نہیں ہو سکتا کیونکہ جب الف سرے سے واجب ہی نہیں تو پھر اس کے واجب ہونے کی کوئی صورت نہیں ہو سکتی لہذا لکن غصب غلط ہو جائیگا پھر کلام متسق نہیں ہو سکتی لہذا الفظ لا نفی سبب ہے نفی واجب نہیں ۔ مقصد یہ ہے کہ بطور قرض نہیں پھر اس کا تدارک کیا یہ تو نے غصب کیا تھا تو اس صورت میں کلام مرتبط ہو جائے گی فلا يكون رداً لا قرارة. یہ رد اقرار نہیں ہوگا بلکہ صرف نفی سبب ہوگی۔ بخلاف ما اذا تزوجت الامة بغير ازن مولدها به غر منسق کی مثال ہے جہاں ما بعد لکن تدارک ماقبل کی صلاحیت نہیں رکھتا وہ یہ کہ ایک مملوکہ بغیر ازن مولیٰ کے یکصد حق المصر کے عوض کسی کے ساتھ نکاح کر لیتی ہے جب مولی کو اطلاع ہوتی ہے تو وہ کہتا ہے لا اجيز النکاح میں اس نکاح کو جائز قرار نہیں دیتا لیکن اجیزه بمائتین لیکن میں اس کو دوصد کے ساتھ جائزہ قرار دیتا ہوں تو اس صورت میں منفسخ النکاح جو نکاح اس لونڈی نے کیا تھا وہ فسخ ہو جائیت کا عن اصلہ یعنی لا اجیز النکاح کے ساتھ اصل نکاح فسخ ہو جا سگا وجعل لكن مبتداء اور لیکن سے کلام مخالف ہو گی جو کہ ماقبل کے ساتھ مرتبط نہیں ہو سکتی لانه لا يمكن اثبات هذا النکاح بمائتیین یعنی اسی نکاح کا جو اصلا فسخ ہو چکا ہے تو اب اجیزہ بمائتین کے ساتھ اس نکاح کا جو عن اصلہ فسخ ہو چکا ہے اثبات بمائتین ممکن نہیں ہے تو اس مسئلہ میں کلام متسق و مربوط نہ رہی ما بعد تدارک ماقبل نہیں ہو سکتا لان الساقة کیوں کہ اس کا اتساق مقتضی ہے کہ ان لا يصح النكاح الأول یعنی جو نکاح اول ہو چکا ہے وہ سرے صحیح نہ رہے لیکن مانتیں کے ساتھ پھر صحیح ہو جائے ڈالا یمکن اور یہ ناممکن ہے لانہ کیونکہ جب اس مولیٰ نے کہا لا اجيز النکاح تو نکاح اول تو سرے سے فسخ ہو جائیگا۔ پھر اس مفسوخ نکاح کا اثبات بمائتین ممکن نہیں ہے۔ فيكون نفى ذلك النکاح کیونکہ ایک ہی نکاح کی نفی پھر بعینہ اسی کا اثبات ہو یہ نہیں ہو سکتا فعلم تو معلوم ہوا کہ یہ کلام غیر مشتق ہے لہذا لیکن اجیزہ بمائتین کو کلام مستانف قرار دیا جائے گا۔ یہ دوسرے نکاح کی اجازت ہوگی جس کی مھر (Then it is established, then secondly some part is excluded, rather both are established together. And based on this they said regarding the one judged in favor of regarding a house by evidence: meaning, on the basis that in the expression of change, the first part of speech is dependent on the latter, and both the first and last are ruled together. So the jurists said: the case of the one judged in favor of regarding a house is that the house was in the possession of Amr, then Bakr brought a claim against him saying 'this house is mine'. Amr denied it, so Bakr established evidence, i.e., witnesses, for his claim. The judge decided the house in favor of Bakr. This is Bakr, the one judged in favor of. Then Bakr says after the judgment: 'This house was never mine, but it is Zaid's'. And Zaid confirms Bakr's statement that the house is Zaid's, but denies Bakr's statement 'it was never mine' and says 'he sold it to me after the judgment' or 'he gifted it to me'. This is meant by 'sold to me' and 'gifted to me after the judgment that the house is for Zaid'. In this case, the house will be Zaid's, and the one judged in favor of, i.e., Bakr, will owe the value of the house to the one judged against, i.e., Amr. Because when he uttered 'lakinnaha' (but it is) contiguously, it is as if he uttered negation and correction together, so both their implications are established together, i.e., denial of ownership for himself and affirmation of ownership for Zaid. Then the necessary consequence is that the witnesses who testified for Bakr are discredited, and ownership is established for the one judged against, i.e., Amr. And this will be established after both statements: denial of self and affirmation of ownership for Zaid. So it is a proof; it will be a proof only against the one judged in favor of, i.e., Bakr, not against Zaid, because this is an admission against himself, which is a limited proof. Therefore, the house will be Zaid's and he will pay the guarantee of price to Amr. Then, the discussion returns to the first point, i.e., that 'lakin' is for correction. Meaning, if the speech is coherent and what follows 'lakin' is related and connected to what precedes, i.e., it is suitable to be a rectification, then it is interpreted as rectification. But if there is no coherence and connection between what precedes and what follows, and what follows 'lakin' does not have the potential for rectification, then it is treated as an independent statement. An example of coherence is: a person admits 'You have one thousand over me as a loan.' Then he says 'No, it is usurpation.' This speech is coherent. So it is correct that it is negation of cause, not negation of obligation. Because his saying 'la' cannot be interpreted as negation of obligation, because if it were interpreted as negation of obligation, i.e., 'the thousand is not obligatory upon me', then the subsequent word 'but usurpation' cannot be correct, because when the thousand is not obligatory at all, there is no way for it to be obligatory, so 'but usurpation' would be wrong and the speech would not be coherent. Therefore, the word 'la' is negation of cause, not negation of obligation. The point is that it is not as a loan, then he rectified by saying you had usurped it. In this case, the speech becomes connected, so it is not a rejection of the admission; rather it is only a negation of cause. Contrast this with the case where a slave girl marries without her master's permission for a dower of one hundred. When the master is informed, he says 'I do not permit the marriage, but I permit it with two hundred.' In this case, the marriage is annulled from its foundation, i.e., with 'I do not permit the marriage' the original marriage is annulled, and the 'but' starts a new statement that is not connected to what precedes, because it is impossible to establish this marriage with two hundred, i.e., this marriage which has already been annulled from its foundation, establishing it with two hundred is impossible. So in this issue, the speech is not coherent and connected; what follows cannot rectify what precedes, because coherence requires that the first marriage not be valid, but then become valid with two hundred, which is impossible. Because when the master said 'I do not permit the marriage', the first marriage is annulled altogether. Then establishing the annulled marriage with two hundred is impossible. Thus, this speech is not coherent. Therefore, 'but I permit it with two hundred' is treated as an independent statement; it is a permission for another marriage with a dower of two hundred. However, in Qadi Khan it is mentioned that if he says 'I do not permit this marriage, but I permit it with two hundred', then the original marriage is not annulled; rather, this is only a rectification in the amount of the dower.)
Source pages p. 349

Commentary
This passage is a usul rule explaining the particle 'lakin' (but) and its legal effect when used for istidrak (correction). The author begins by establishing that when 'lakin' is used contiguously (muttasil) with the preceding statement, both parts—the negation and the affirmation—are established simultaneously. He provides the case of a house dispute: Bakr wins a judgment based on evidence, but then says 'it was never mine, but it is Zaid's.' Because 'lakin' connects the two statements, Bakr's denial of ownership for himself and his affirmation of Zaid's ownership both take effect. Consequently, the house goes to Zaid, but Bakr must pay its value to Amr (the original possessor) because Bakr's admission against himself is a limited proof. The author then revisits the rule: 'lakin' is interpreted as istidrak only if the speech is coherent (mustaqim) and the latter part can rectify (tadaruk) the former. If the speech lacks coherence, the part after 'lakin' is treated as a new independent statement. Two examples illustrate this: coherent case—a person says 'you have 1000 as a loan' then 'no, it is usurpation.' Here 'no' negates the cause (loan), not the obligation, so the speech is coherent and the admission stands with the correction. Incoherent case—a master says 'I do not permit the marriage, but I permit it with 200.' The first part annuls the marriage, so the second cannot rectify it; thus, it becomes a new offer for a different marriage. An exception from Qadi Khan: if the master explicitly says 'I do not permit this marriage, but I permit it with 200,' the original marriage is not annulled; instead, the 'but' serves to rectify the dower amount only. This nuanced discussion demonstrates the Hanafi method of analyzing linguistic particles in legal contexts.

Key Terms
لکن (lakin): A particle indicating istidrak (correction) when the speech is coherent and the latter part can rectify the former.
استدراك (istidrak): Rectification or correction of a preceding statement by a subsequent one connected via 'lakin'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the marriage case, why is the general example considered incoherent?
A) Because the master changes his mind.
B) Because the first part annuls the marriage, and the second part cannot rectify a non-existent marriage.
C) Because 'lakin' is not used correctly.
D) Because the dower amounts differ.

Key Takeaway
The loan example is coherent and both statements stand; the marriage example is incoherent and the 'but' clause starts a new statement, except when wording explicitly references the same marriage (Qadi Khan).

The Legal Meaning of 'Aw' (Or)
Defines the particle 'aw' and its legal implications when connecting nouns or sentences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the legal effect of the particle 'aw' and distinguish its application when connecting singular nouns versus sentences.

Core Idea
The particle 'aw' always indicates one of the options, not a combination.

Understanding the particle 'aw' is crucial in legal language because it determines whether a ruling applies to all or some. In Hanafi usul, 'aw' is treated as tab'id (division), unlike 'waw' which is jam' (combination). This lesson explains its implications when connecting nouns or sentences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the particle and its function
Locate the Arabic particle 'aw' in a legal statement and recognize that it serves to divide options.
2
Distinguish between connecting singular nouns vs sentences
When 'aw' connects two singular nouns (mufradayn), it gives the ruling for one of them. When it connects two sentences (jumlatayn), it indicates that one of the two meanings holds.
3
Apply to a legal example
Given a contract, oath, or bequest using 'aw', determine which item is intended or how the ruling applies.
For example, 'Sell me this or that' gives the buyer a choice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
او لاحد الشائن یعنی کلمہ اوشین میں سے کسی ایک کے لئے ہے جب مفردین کے مابین داخل ہوگا تو ثبوت حکم لاحد ما کا افادہ کرے گا اگر جملتین کے درمیان داخل ہو تو پھر یہ افادہ کرے گا کہ ان دو میں سے کسی ایک کا مضمون حاصل ہے اور جب اشیاء کثیرہ میں داخل ہو تو پھر ثبوت لاحد الاشیاء کا افادہ کریگا
('Aw' is for one of the two things, meaning the word 'aw' is for one of two. When it occurs between two singular nouns, it indicates the establishment of the ruling for one of them. If it occurs between two sentences, then it indicates that the meaning of one of the two is attained. And when it occurs among many things, then it indicates the establishment for one of the things.)
Source pages p. 350

Commentary
This passage is a usul definition of the particle 'aw' (or). The author states that 'aw' is used to indicate one of the enumerated items. When it connects two singular nouns (mufradayn), the ruling applies to one of the two, not both. For example, if someone says 'sell me this or that,' the buyer has the right to choose one. When 'aw' connects two sentences (jumlatayn), it indicates that one of the two meanings is established. For instance, if a person says 'I owe you a thousand or I owe you a house,' only one of the debts is established. When 'aw' is used among many items (ashya' kathirah), it similarly indicates one of them. This definition is foundational in Hanafi usul for understanding legal language, especially in contracts, oaths, and bequests, where 'aw' creates an option rather than a combination.

Key Terms
أو (aw): A particle indicating that the ruling applies to one of the connected items, not all.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When 'aw' occurs between two sentences, what does it indicate?
A) Both sentences are true.
B) One of the two meanings holds.
C) The first sentence is canceled.
D) The second sentence is the only valid one.

Key Takeaway
The particle 'aw' in legal language always indicates one of the connected items, never all.

Aw (أو) as Ghayah: The Rule of Endpoint in Hanafi Usul
Explaining the usage of aw meaning hatta and its application in Quranic exegesis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when 'aw' functions as 'hatta' (until) in Quranic verses and oaths, and apply the Hanafi usul principle to derive the correct meaning.

Core Idea
When aw terminates a prior state, it means 'until' — the endpoint removes the coexistent condition.

In Hanafi usul, particles are not static; their meaning shifts with intent. This lesson examines the particle 'aw' (أو) when it takes the meaning of 'hatta' (حتى, until). Using the famous example from Surah Al Imran 3:128, we see how the Hanafi school resolves an apparent contradiction by interpreting 'aw' as an endpoint (ghayah) that removes a prior state. This principle applies to oaths and conditional statements, offering a precise tool for legal exegesis.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the linguistic analogy
Understand that with 'hatta', what precedes it is a coexistent state (mu'ayyan) and what follows is its endpoint (ghayah). The same structure applies to 'aw' when it means 'until'.
The analogy is key: 'aw' functions like 'hatta' in discontinuing the first act.
2
Identify the problem in the Quranic verse
Read Quran 3:128: 'You have no part in the matter — either He turns to them in mercy or punishes them.' If 'aw' means 'or', then the Prophet's lack of part ends when either event occurs, contradicting divine sovereignty. Recognize this as the problem that prompted the analysis.
The verse is من المتشابهات (ambiguous) without proper usul interpretation.
3
Analyze the two Hanafi interpretations
The passage offers two tawjih: (1) The verse removed the Prophet's distress over his wounds; (2) It prohibited a prolonged supplication for destruction. Both preserve 'aw' as 'hatta' indicating the endpoint of the distress or prohibition.
These interpretations show how context and intent determine linguistic meaning.
4
Apply the rule to the oath example
Consider the oath: 'I will stay with you until you give me my right' (لا ألزمنك أو تعطيني حقي). The obligation to stay is removed when the right is given, just as the coexistent state is removed by the endpoint.
This demonstrates practical application in Hanafi fiqh of oaths (al-ayman).
5
Formulate the usul principle
State the rule: When an act (ma qabl) is intended to be discontinued by a subsequent act (ma ba'd), 'aw' takes the meaning of 'hatta', making the second act the endpoint that nullifies the first.
This principle guides muftis in interpreting ambiguous texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
انقطاع اس فعل سے مقصود ہو جو واقع بعد از او ہے تو ایسی صورتوں میں عطف نہیں ہو سکتا ابدا حتی کے معنی میں کیا جاتا ہے جیسے کہ ماقبل حتی معیا ہوتا ہے اور ما بعد حتی غایتہ ہوتی ہے تو وجود ناتے کے ساتھ معیا مرتفع ہو جاتا ہے یہاں بھی ایسے ہے لان احدهما يرتفع بوجود الاخریعنی ان معطوفين میں سے ایک کے ساتھ دوسرا مرتفع ہو جاتا ہے اسی مناسبت سے او بمعنی حتی ہو جاتا ہے جیسے لالزمنك او تعطینی حق میں لزوم ممتدر ہو سکتا ہے جب ادائیگی حق ہو جائیگی تو وہ لزوم مرتفع ہو جائیگا۔ جیسے وجود غایتہ کے ساتھ مفیا مرتفع ہو جاتا ہے۔ اب آیت قرآنیہ میں یہ اشکال ہے کہ لیس لک من الا درشتی اگر چہ یہ ممتد تو ہے کیا ادیتوب علیہم اما بعد بہم کے ساتھ مرتفع ہو سکتا ہے یعنی جب اللہ تعالیٰ ان مشرکین کو توفیق تو به دیدے کہ وہ اسلام قبول کر لیں یا مشرکین کو بحالت شرک بلاک کر دے اور عذاب میں ڈال دے تو کیا لیس لک من الامرشی ختم ہو جائے گا اور امر حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے قبضہ و اختیار میں آجائے گا حالانکہ ایسے نہیں ہے جیسے اللہ الا مر من قبل ومن بعد اور آیتہ مذکورہ کا آخر واللہ مانی السموات وما فی الارض اس پر دال ہے کہ یہ امر و معاملہ جمیع اوقات میں اللہ تعالیٰ کے قبضہ اور ملک میں ہے۔ تو اس اشکال کو مرتفع کرنے میں دو تو جہیں کی جاتی ہیں ایک یہ کہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم جب غزوہ احد میں زخمی ہوئے تو سخت پریشانی کے عالم میں کیف یفلح قوم او موادجہ نبیہم کہا اور اس کے ساتھ فرمایا اللهم العن ابا سفیان و حارث بن ہشام و سهیل ابن عمرو و صفوان ابن امیه تو يه انتهانی پریشانی کے عالم میں تھی تو اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا لیس لک من الامر شی او تیوب علیهم او بعد مبہم تو ان دونوں صورتوں کے ساتھ ازالہ پریشانی کیا گیا معنی یہ ہوا کہ حتی بتوب علیہم فتفرح بحالهم او بعد بهم فتشفى منهم تو گویالیس لک دال ہوا اضطراب و پریشانی پر جو ما بعد او کے ساتھ مرتفع ہوئی جیسے معیا مرتفع بالغایتہ ہوتا ہے تو او بمعنی حتی ہوگا۔ ثانیا یہ کہ لیس لک من الامرشتی کے ساتھ دعا مہلاک الاعدامہ کی تحریم کی گئی ہے جو کہ محتمل امتداد تھی اس لئے او کو غایتہ کے معنی پر محمول کیا جائے گا جیسے امر ممتد کو غایتہ کے ساتھ منتہی کیا جاتا ہے یہاں بھی ایسے ہے کیونکہ اگر وہ مسلمان ہو گئے تو بھی بددعا نہیں ہوگی اگر بلاک ہو گئے تو بھی مقصود حاصل ہوا نہ بددعا کی ضرورت ہے اور نہ اس کی تحریم کا امتداد ۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب۔
The discontinuation is intended from that act which occurs after aw, so in such cases conjunction cannot occur at all; it is taken in the meaning of hatta. Just as what is before hatta is coexistent and what is after hatta is its endpoint, so with the existence of the endpoint the coexistent is removed. Here it is also like that because one of them is removed by the existence of the other. That is, among the two conjoined items, the second is removed with the first. On this basis, aw takes the meaning of hatta, as in 'I will surely stay with you until you give me my right': the staying can be extended, and when the payment of the right occurs, that staying is removed, just as the coexistent is removed with the existence of the endpoint. Now in the Quranic verse there is this difficulty: 'You have no part in the matter' — although this is extended, can it be removed by 'until He turns to them in mercy or punishes them'? That is, if Allah grants them the success to accept Islam or blocks the polytheists in their state of polytheism and punishes them, then will 'you have no part in the matter' cease and the matter come into the control of the Prophet (PBUH)? But this is not the case, as 'To Allah belongs the command before and after' and the end of the mentioned verse 'and to Allah belongs whatever is in the heavens and whatever is on the earth' indicate that this command and affair is in Allah's control and dominion at all times. So to remove this difficulty, two interpretations are given: First, that when the Prophet (PBUH) was wounded in the Battle of Uhud, in a state of great distress he said 'How can a people succeed who have stained their Prophet's face?' and along with that he said 'O Allah, curse Abu Sufyan, Harith ibn Hisham, Suhayl ibn Amr, and Safwan ibn Umayyah.' This was in a state of extreme distress, so Allah said 'You have no part in the matter — either He turns to them in mercy or punishes them.' Thus removal of distress was made through these two possibilities, meaning 'until He turns to them in mercy and you rejoice in their state, or punishes them and you are avenged of them.' So 'you have no part' indicates distress, which is removed with what is after aw, just as the coexistent is removed by the endpoint, so aw is in the meaning of hatta. Second, that 'you have no part in the matter' prohibits the supplication for the destruction of enemies, which was likely to be prolonged. Therefore, aw is interpreted to mean the endpoint, just as an extended matter is terminated by its endpoint. Here it is like that because if they become Muslims, the supplication will not be made; if they are punished, the objective is achieved. There is no need for the supplication nor for its prolongation. And Allah knows best the correct opinion.
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This passage is a usul rule explaining the particle 'aw' (أو) when it takes the meaning of 'hatta' (حتى, until). The author begins by stating that when an act is intended to be discontinued by a subsequent act, 'aw' cannot function as a conjunction (عطف) but instead means 'hatta'. The analogy is that what precedes 'hatta' is a state that coexists (معيا) with its condition, and what follows 'hatta' is its endpoint (غاية), so the coexistent state is removed by the arrival of the endpoint. Similarly, 'aw' here indicates that one of two conjoined items is removed by the existence of the other. For example, in 'I will surely stay with you until you give me my right' (لا ألزمنك أو تعطيني حقي), the obligation to stay is removed when the right is paid. The author then applies this to the Quranic verse 3:128: 'You have no part in the matter — either He turns to them in mercy or punishes them.' The apparent problem is that if 'aw' means 'until', then when either repentance or punishment occurs, the Prophet's 'no part' would end, implying control over the affair, contradicting verse 3:154 and the end of the same verse. Two interpretations are given: (1) The Prophet's distress over his wounds led to his supplication, and Allah revealed this verse to remove that distress by giving two possible outcomes (repentance or punishment), so 'aw' means 'until' the distress ends. (2) The prohibition of supplication for destruction is a prolonged matter, so 'aw' indicates its endpoint. Both interpretations preserve the meaning of 'aw' as 'hatta'.

Key Terms
أو (aw): A particle that can mean 'or' for conjunction, or 'until' (بمعنى حتى) when the first act is intended to be discontinued by the second.
غاية (ghayah): Endpoint or limit; that which terminates a preceding state or action.
معیا (mu'ayyan / ma'iyya): A coexistent state that remains until removed by its endpoint.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the example 'I will surely stay with you until you give me my right' (لا ألزمنك أو تعطيني حقي), what is the meaning of 'aw'?
A) Conjunction (or) – the person can either stay or not stay.
B) Choice – the person has the option to stay or leave.
C) Until (hatta) – the obligation to stay ends when the right is given.
D) Explanation – clarifying that the right will be given.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, 'aw' can mean 'hatta' (until) when the preceding act is meant to be discontinued by the following one, making it a powerful tool for interpreting Quranic verses and legal oaths.

The Particle 'Aw' as 'Hatta' in Oaths: A Hanafi Usul Rule
Ruling on an oath involving aw in the sense of ghayah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when the particle 'aw' in a negated oath indicates ghayah (until) and derive the correct ruling on hanath.

Core Idea
In Hanafi usul, 'aw' after a negation followed by a mansub verb indicates ghayah, not choice.

This lesson unpacks a specific usul rule applied to oaths: the particle 'aw' can function as 'hatta' (until) rather than as a conjuction. By examining the grammatical structure of the oath, we derive the Hanafi ruling on when the oath is broken (hanath). This example from the classical texts illustrates how grammatical analysis informs legal interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the oath and the key particle
Consider the oath: 'I will not enter this house or I will enter that house.' Note the presence of 'aw' between a negation and a positive verb.
The Arabic: لا أدخل هذه الدار أو أدخل تلك الدار
2
Perform grammatical analysis
The verb after 'aw' (أدخل) is mansub (subjunctive). There is no preceding mansub verb. Therefore, 'aw' cannot be a conjunction ('atf); it must be interpreted as 'hatta' (until).
Hanafi linguists: if 'aw' is followed by a mansub without a preceding mansub, it indicates ghayah.
3
Apply the rule to determine the legal meaning
The negation 'I will not enter this house' is a coexistent state that continues until the endpoint: entry into that house. So the oath means 'I will not enter this house until I enter that house.'
The non-entry is prolonged (ممتد) until the second entry.
4
Derive the ruling on hanath
If he enters the second house first, the coexistent state is removed at its endpoint, so the oath is fulfilled. If he enters the first house first, he breaks the oath because he entered before the endpoint.
Entering the first house first violates the oath (حنث); entering the second first fulfills it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان حلف لا ادخل هذه الدار او ادخل تلك الدار تو اس کلام کے اندراو کے بعد لفظ ادخل مضارع منصوب ہے اس سے قبل مضارع منصوب نہیں ہے لہذا خطف نہیں ہو سکتا تو اس صورت میں دار اولیٰ کا عدم دخول ممتد رہے گا دخول ثانیہ تک نان دخل الدولى اولاً حنث کیونکہ اس صورت میں عدم دخول اولی جو معیا تھا وہ اپنی غایتہ دخول ثانیہ کے ساتھ مرتفع ہو سکتا تھا اس سے قبل نہیں تو جب اس کے خلاف کیا تو حانث ہو جائے گا۔ اگر نانیہ میں اولا داخل ہوتا ہے تو ہر فی یمینہ یعنی اس کی قسم پوری ہوگئی ہے کیوں کہ معطوف علیہ منتہی ہو چکا ہے اب دار اولی میں داخل ہونے کے ساتھ مانٹ نہیں ہو گا
If he swears 'I will not enter this house or I will enter that house', then in this statement after 'aw' the word 'enter' is a mansub mudari; before it there is no mansub mudari, therefore conjunction ('atf) is not possible. So in this case, non-entry into the first house will be prolonged until entry into the second. If he enters the second first, he breaks the oath because in this case the non-entry into the first, which was a coexistent state, could be removed only by its endpoint, the entry into the second, not before. So when he did the opposite, he is an oath-breaker. If he enters the second first, his oath is fulfilled because the conjoined item has reached its endpoint; now entering the first house will not cause an oath-break.
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This passage is a fiqh example illustrating the previous usul rule about 'aw' meaning 'hatta'. The author considers an oath: 'I will not enter this house or I will enter that house.' The grammatical analysis shows that 'aw' is followed by a mansub verb (أدخل), and there is no mansub verb before it, so 'aw' cannot be a conjunction ('atf). Therefore, 'aw' here means 'hatta' (until). The ruling: the non-entry into the first house is a coexistent state that is intended to last until entry into the second house. If the person enters the second house first, the non-entry into the first is removed at that endpoint, so he broke the oath by entering the first? Actually careful: The text says if he enters the second first, he breaks the oath because he violated the non-entry before the endpoint? Wait: The text says: 'If he enters the second first, he breaks the oath because... the non-entry into the first could only be removed by entry into the second, not before.' So the oath is that he will not enter the first until he enters the second. If he enters the second first, the non-entry into the first is still ongoing? Actually the ruling is: he intended to not enter the first until he enters the second. If he enters the second first, he has removed the coexistent non-entry of the first? The text says he holds (حنث) because he did the opposite: he entered the first? Let's read: 'نان دخل الدولى اولاً حنث' – 'if he enters the first first, he breaks the oath.' Actually the text: 'اگر نانیہ میں اولا داخل ہوتا ہے تو ہر فی یمینہ' – 'if he enters the second first, his oath is fulfilled.' So the correct ruling: If he enters the first house first, he breaks the oath because he entered before the endpoint (the second house). If he enters the second house first, the oath is fulfilled because the condition (non-entry until second) is satisfied. The commentary should clarify this Hanafi ruling.

Key Terms
حنث (hanath): The act of breaking an oath; the legal consequence of violating a sworn statement.
یمین (yamin): An oath; a solemn declaration invoking Allah's name to emphasize a statement or promise.
غایة (ghayah): Endpoint or limit; in oaths, the condition that when reached removes the coexistent state.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone swears 'I will not enter house A or I will enter house B' (meaning 'until I enter B'), and then enters house B first, what is the ruling?
A) He breaks the oath because he entered before house A.
B) He fulfills the oath; the non-entry into A is removed by entering B.
C) The oath is invalid because 'aw' creates confusion.
D) He must enter both houses to fulfill the oath.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the particle 'aw' in a negated oath functions as 'hatta' (until), making entry before the endpoint a break of the oath.

Uses of Ḥatta (حتى): Ghāyah, ʿAṭf, and Ibtidā'
Grammar/usul rule: explaining three functions of ḥatta

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and distinguish the three uses of ḥatta (ghāyah, ʿaṭf, ibtidā') and apply the conditions for each when interpreting legal texts.

Core Idea
Ḥatta can indicate endpoint, conjunction, or inceptive; each use has distinct conditions affecting legal interpretation.

The particle ḥatta (حتى) carries multiple functions in Arabic, and correctly identifying its use is crucial for usūl al-fiqh. This passage, from a classical Hanafi work, breaks down the three primary uses: ghāyah (endpoint), ʿaṭf (conjunction), and ibtidā' (inceptive). Each imposes specific conditions on the preceding and following elements, and these conditions can change the legal ruling extracted from a text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the particle ḥatta in the text
Locate the occurrence of ḥatta and determine the context: is it followed by a noun, a verb, or a new clause?
The surrounding linguistic clues will help classify it.
2
Check for ghāyah (endpoint)
If ḥatta indicates the termination of the preceding action or state, it is ghāyah. Ask: does the action stop at this point? The post-hatta element may or may not be part of the preceding thing.
3
Check for ʿaṭf (conjunction)
If the post-hatta element agrees in declension with the preceding, consider conjunction. Conditions: same genus, and the conjoined item must be superior or inferior. Also, the preceding action must occur gradually.
This is common in legal texts where exceptions are made.
4
Check for ibtidā' (inceptive)
If ḥatta starts a new sentence independent of the previous clause, it is ibtidā'. It can be a verbal or nominal sentence. For nominal sentences, either the predicate is mentioned or estimated from the context.
This often introduces a new consideration.
5
Apply the correct interpretation in legal analysis
The identified use of ḥatta determines how the text's ruling is bounded or extended. For example, ghāyah sets a limit, ʿaṭf includes an item under the same ruling, and ibtidā' introduces an independent statement.
This directly affects the derivation of fiqh rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حتى للغاية یعنی لفظ حتی برائے غایتہ ہے یعنی مینیا اس پر سپہونچ کر منتہی ہوگا نحوحتی مطلع لفجر تو نزول ملائکہ طلوع فجر بر منتہی ہو جاتا ہے رحتی راسما جیسے اکلت السمكة حتى راسها تو فعل اكل راسها فجربر تک پہونچ کر منتہی ہوا اور مابعد حتی کبھی ماقبل کی جز ہوتا ہے جیسے حتی راسھا اور کبھی جز نہیں ہوتا جیسے مطلع الفجرين وقد تجئ للعطف یعنی کبھی لفظ حتی برائے عطف آتا ہے تو اس وقت ما بعد حتی اعراب میں ماقبل کے تابع ہوگا اور عاطفہ کے اندر یہ شرط ہے کہ معطوف جنز ہو معطوف علیہ کی اور فضل من الاجزاء ہو یا اخس اور ادون ہو اور جو ماقبل حتی کے اندر حکم موجود ہے اس کے لئے شرط ہے کہ منقضی شیئا فشیاء یعنی آہستہ آہستہ ہوتا اور گزرتا جائے یہاں تک کہ معطوف تک منتہی ہو لیکن یہ انتہا اعتبار متکلم کے لحاظ سے ہوتی ہے یعنی متکلم اپنے ذہن میں ترتیب و تدریج کو من الاضعف الى الاقوى یا بالعکس ملحوظ رکھتا ہے نفس الامر اور عالم وجود میں یہ ترتیب ضروری نہیں کہ ایسے ہو جیسے متکلم نے ذھنا اختیار کی ہے نفس الامر میں کبھی یوں ہوتا ہے کہ حکم معطوف کے ساتھ اولاً تعلق پکڑتا ہے اور معطوف علیہ کے ساتھ ثانیا جیسے مات کل اپ کی حتی آدم اور کبھی معطوف کے ساتھ حکم متعلق ہوتا ہے فی وسط المعطوف علیہ جیسے مات الناس حتى الانبياء - وتدخل على جملة مبتدأة ير حتى ابتدائیہ کہلاتا ہے ایسے جملہ پر داخل ہوتا ہے جو از سر نو شروع ہو رہا ہے نہ غایتہ ہے نہ عطف یہ کبھی جملہ فعلیہ ہو گا اور کبھی اسمیہ اور اسمیہ ہونے کی صورت میں نان ذكر الخبر اگر خبر مبتدا مذکور ہو جیسے ضربت القوم حتى زيد غضبان یہ حتی ابتدئیه ہے جملہ اسمیہ زید عضبان پر داخل ہے غضبان خبر ہے جو کہ مذکور ہے ۔ جواب الشرط ههنا محذوف یعنی لفظ ان ذكر الخبر شرط ہے اور اس کا جواب محذوف ہے۔ ای فبها و نعمت یہ ہے جواب شرط جو محذوف ہے معنی اس کا یہ ہے فمرحبا بالقضیہ ونعمت القضیہ یعنی جو خبر مذکور ہے پس وہی بہتر ہے اور ٹھیک اور درست ہے اونا لخبر ذلك يا جواب شرط ہے فالخبر ذالک جو محذوف ہے یعنی جو مذکور ہے پس وہی اس کی خبر ہے والد اگر جملہ اسمیہ جس پر حتی داخل ہے اس میں خبر مذکور نہیں ہے تو یقدر من جنس یعنی جنس ما تقدم یعنی جنس ما قبل سے مقدر کی جائیگی نحوا كلت السمكة حتى را شها برفع الراس تو یہ مبتدا ہے اور خبر اس کی از جنس ما قبل مقدر ہے یعنی حتی راسها ما كول وان دخلت الافعال اگر حتی افعال پر داخل ہو تو یہ تین قسم ہوتا ہے کبھی برائے غایتہ ہوتا
Hatta for ghayah: that is, the word hatta is for the endpoint, meaning the coexistent [state] reaches it and ends. Example: 'until the break of dawn' – the descent of angels ends at the break of dawn. Another example: 'I ate the fish until its head' – the action of eating reached its head and ended. And what is after hatta is sometimes part of what precedes, like 'until its head', and sometimes not part, like 'until the break of dawn'. And it sometimes comes for 'atf (conjunction): that is, sometimes the word hatta is for conjunction, then what is after hatta will follow what precedes in declension, and the condition for it being a conjunction is that the conjoined item be of the same genus as the first and be superior in parts or inferior and lesser. And for the ruling present in what is before hatta, the condition is that it occurs gradually, one thing after another, until it reaches the conjoined item. But this endpoint is from the speaker's perspective: the speaker in his mind observes an order and gradation from weaker to stronger or vice versa. In actual reality, this order does not have to be as the speaker mentally assumed; in reality, sometimes the ruling attaches first to the conjoined item and second to the first, like 'everyone died, even Adam', and sometimes the ruling attaches to the conjoined item in the middle of the first, like 'people died, even the prophets'. And it enters upon a new sentence: that which is called ibtida'iyyah (initial hatta). It enters upon a sentence that starts anew, not being an endpoint nor a conjunction. It is sometimes a verbal sentence and sometimes a nominal sentence. In the case of a nominal sentence, if the predicate of the subject is mentioned, e.g., 'I beat the people, and Zayd was angry' – this is ibtida'iyyah hatta: it enters upon the nominal sentence 'Zayd was angry', and 'angry' is the predicate which is mentioned. The answer to the condition here is omitted: that is, the phrase 'if the predicate is mentioned' is the condition, and its answer is omitted. That is, 'so it is good and excellent' – this is the answer to the condition, which is omitted. Its meaning is: 'so welcome to the matter, and excellent matter' – i.e., the predicate that is mentioned, so it is better and correct. Or 'the predicate is that' – so the predicate is that, which is omitted – i.e., what is mentioned, so it is its predicate. And if the nominal sentence upon which hatta enters does not have a predicate mentioned, then it is estimated from the same genus, i.e., the genus of what preceded. Example: 'I ate the fish until its head' with raf' of 'head' – so this is a subject and its predicate is estimated from the genus of what preceded, i.e., 'until its head is eaten'. And if hatta enters upon verbs, it is of three types: sometimes it is for ghayah...
Source pages p. 359

Commentary
This passage is a detailed grammatical and usul analysis of the particle 'hatta' (حتى). The author distinguishes three uses:

1. **Hatta for ghayah (endpoint)**: It indicates the termination of a preceding action or state. The preceding coexistent state reaches the endpoint and ends. The post-hatta element may or may not be part of the preceding thing. Example: 'I ate the fish until its head' – the head is part of the fish; 'until the break of dawn' – dawn is not part of the descent of angels.

2. **Hatta for 'atf (conjunction)**: Here the post-hatta element follows the preceding in declension. Conditions: (a) the conjoined item must be of the same genus as the first, and (b) it must be either superior in parts or inferior and lesser. Additionally, the ruling in the preceding part must occur gradually, thing after thing, until reaching the conjoined item. However, this gradation is according to the speaker's intention; in actual reality, the order may differ. Examples: 'Everyone died, even Adam' – where the ruling of death applies to Adam more strongly; 'People died, even the prophets' – where the prophets are singled out within the people.

3. **Hatta for ibtida' (initial/inceptive)**: This hatta enters upon a new sentence, neither as an endpoint nor as a conjunction. It can be a verbal or nominal sentence. For nominal sentences, if the predicate is mentioned, it is explicit; if not, it is estimated from the context. The author gives an example: 'I beat the people, when Zayd was angry' – here the hatta is ibtida'iyyah. There is a conditional statement: 'if the predicate is mentioned' has an omitted answer meaning 'so it is good'. Also, if the predicate is not mentioned, it is estimated from the genus of what preceded, as in 'I ate the fish until its head' (with raf') – the predicate is 'eaten'.

The passage concludes by noting that when hatta enters upon verbs, it has three types, one of which is for ghayah (but the text is cut off).

Key Terms
حتى (hatta): A particle with multiple uses: (1) ghayah – indicating endpoint; (2) 'atf – conjunction with conditions; (3) ibtida' – entering upon a new sentence.
غاية (ghayah): The endpoint or limit at which a preceding action or state terminates.
عطف ('atf): Grammatical conjunction; here specifically for hatta where the post-hatta element follows in declension.
ابتداء (ibtida'): Inceptive; hatta that begins a new sentence unrelated to the preceding clause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which condition must be satisfied for hatta to function as a conjunction ('atf)?
A) The conjoined item must be of a different genus than the first.
B) The conjoined item must be superior or inferior in relation to the first.
C) The preceding action must be instantaneous.
D) The post-hatta element must be in the accusative case.

Key Takeaway
The particle hatta has three distinct uses (ghayah, 'atf, ibtida') each with specific conditions that critically affect the interpretation of legal texts.

The Particle حتى in Hanafi Legal Analysis
Analyzing the legal usages of the Arabic particle حتى in oaths and Quranic verses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three functions of the particle هatta (ghaya, sababiyya, 'ataf) in Quranic and oath contexts, and apply the Hanafi conditions to determine which function is operative in a given legal statement.

Core Idea
اللفظ حتى يحمل على الغاية، السببية، أو العطف بحسب السياق وإمكان الامتداد — الخلط بينها يغير الحكم في اليمين.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi usul analysis of the Arabic particle هatta (حتى). In legal texts, especially oaths and conditional statements, the correct interpretation of hatta determines whether a person violates their oath. Hanafi scholars distinguish three uses: ghaya (limit), sababiyya (cause), and 'ataf (mere conjunction). The classification depends on whether the preceding action can extend and whether the following action serves as a natural endpoint. Understanding these criteria equips you to derive the correct legal ruling from texts containing هatta.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three legal functions of هatta
List the three uses: ghaya (limit), sababiyya (cause), 'ataf (conjunction). Each carries different conditions.
Refer to the legal definition dissector below.
2
Apply the condition for ghaya
For ghaya, the preceding action must admit extension (imtidad) and the following action must be a natural endpoint (nihaya). Test the example 'hatta yu'tu al-jizya': fighting can extend; accepting jizya ends it.
If these hold, hatta is ghaya.
3
Apply the condition for sababiyya
If ghaya fails, check if the preceding action can be a cause for the following. Example: 'aslamtu hatta adkhula al-jannah' – accepting Islam causes entry to Paradise, but entry does not end Islam; it strengthens it.
If cause is possible, hatta is sababiyya.
4
Identify pure 'ataf
If neither ghaya nor sababiyya applies, hatta is mere conjunction. Both actions must exist for inclusion. Example: 'in lam atika hatta al-ghada' 'indaka' – coming and food being present are conjoined.
For 'ataf, the condition is that the conjuncted is of the same genus and less significant.
5
Apply to an oath scenario
Given an oath like 'I will not strike you until you shout', determine whether stopping before shouting violates the oath. Use the ghaya analysis: striking admits extension; shouting is the end; so stopping before shouting violates.
This demonstrates the practical consequence.

والد کیعنی اگر صدر احتمال امتداد اور آخر منتہی بننے کی صلاحیت نہ رکھتا ہو تو پھر دیکھا جائے گا خان صلح لان يكون سببا للثانی یعنی اگر صدر اس فعل کیلئے جو حتی کے بعد سبب بننے کی صلاحیت رکھتا ہو تو یہ حتی بمعنی گئی ہو گا جو دال علی السبیہ ہے کیونکہ جزا اور مسبب چونکہ مقصود من الشئی ہوتا ہے اس لئے بمنزلہ غایتہ کے ہوگا ۔ نحو اسلمت حتى ادخل الجنة یہاں غایتہ کا معنی نہیں ہو سکتا کیونکہ اگر اسلمت سے مراد احداث اسلام ہے تو اس میں امتداد نہیں ہے اور اگر ثبات على الاسلام مراد ہے تو دخول جنتہ اس کے منتہی اور مقام انقطاع بننے کی صلاحیت نہیں رکھتا بلکہ دخول جنتہ کیساتھ اسلام اثبت اور اقومی ہو جائے گا لہذا یہاں حتی برائے سببیہ ہو گا والا فل لعطف یعنی اگر صدر یعنی ماقبل حتی ثانی کے لئے یعنی ما بعد حتی کے لئے سبب نہ بن سکے تو وہ حتی عطف محض کیلئے ہوگا لا للغایتہ ولا للسببیہ اور عطف محض میں وجود فعلین شرط ہے تاکہ تشریک متحقق ہو جو مقتضائے عطف ہے خان قال عبدى حد ان لم اضربك یه توضیح بالا مثلہ ہے اب یہ مثال غایتہ کی ہے یعنی حتی تصمیم میں حتی براتے غایتہ ہے کیونکہ صدر کلام یعنی ضرب محتمل امتداد ہے اور حتی تصیح صلاحیت برائے انتہا رکھتا ہے کیونکہ صباح مضروب عموماً ضرب کے لئے منتہی بن جاتا ہے تو اس مثال میں حقی برائے عایشہ ہے اگر اس نے صباح مضروب سے پہلے اپنی ضرب روک لی تو وہ حانث ہو جائے گا اور بعد ازار ہو جائیگا۔ اگر یہاں تک مارتا رہا کہ مضروب نے چیخ پکار کی تو پھر حانث نہیں ہوگا۔ وان قال عبدی حران لم انك حتى تفدینی اس مثال میں حتی برائے سببیہ ہے برائے غایتہ نہیں ہے کیونکہ آخر کلام یعنی تفریہ ماقبل کے لئے یعنی انسان کے لئے انتہامہ بننے کی صلاحیت نہیں رکھتا بلکہ یہ داعی الی الاتیان ہے اور اتیان صلاحیت سببیہ رکھتا ہے اور غدا جز ابن سکتی ہے لہذا یہ محمول علی السبیہ ہو گا ۔ فاتاہ فلم بغده لم يحنث اگر اس شخص کے آنے پر مخاطب نے غذا نہیں دی تو حانث نہیں ہو گا ۔ کیونکہ یہ بصورت غایت ہو سکتا ہے اور یہاں غایت کا معنی ہو نہیں سکتا ۔ ولو قال حتی الغدی عندک یعنی وہ کہتا ہے ان لم اتک حتی القدس عندک تو اس مثال میں حتی صرف برائے عطف
What was intended could be elevated with its limit of second entry, not before, so when he opposed it, he becomes a violator (hanith). If he first enters the first house, then his oath is fulfilled, because the conjuncted (ma'tuf 'alayh) has ended, so now entering the first house does not cause violation. Hatta for ghaya: meaning the word hatta is for limit, i.e., the intended action reaches it and ends, like 'until the break of dawn' (hatta matla' al-fajr): the descent of angels ends at dawn. Like 'I ate the fish until its head' (akaltu al-samakata hatta ra'siha): the action of eating the head ended at reaching it. And what comes after hatta is sometimes part of what precedes, as in 'until its head', and sometimes not part, as in 'until the break of dawn'. And it sometimes comes for 'ataf (conjunction): that is, sometimes hatta comes for conjunction, then what follows hatta follows what precedes in grammatical inflection, and the condition for conjunction is that the conjuncted be of the same type as the conjuncted-to, and be a part or less significant. And the ruling existing in what precedes hatta must occur gradually, piece by piece, until it reaches the conjuncted. But this ending is according to the speaker's consideration; the speaker mentally observes order and gradation from weaker to stronger or vice versa; in reality this order is not necessary. Sometimes in reality the ruling attaches to the conjuncted first and to the conjuncted-to second, as in 'everyone died until Adam'; and sometimes the ruling attaches to the conjuncted in the middle of the conjuncted-to, as in 'the people died until the prophets'. And it enters on an independent clause: hatta ibtida'iyyah is called, it enters on a clause that starts anew, not as ghaya nor 'ataf. Sometimes it is a verbal clause, sometimes nominal. When nominal, if the khabar is mentioned, e.g., 'I struck the people until Zaid was angry' (darabtu al-qawma hatta Zaydun ghadban): this is hatta ibtida'iyyah on the nominal clause Zaydun ghadban, with ghadban as the mentioned khabar. The answer to the condition here is omitted: the word 'in' (if) for mentioning the khabar is the condition, and its answer is omitted, i.e., 'fa biha wa ni'mat' is the answer of the condition, meaning 'welcome to the proposition, and what an excellent proposition' – that is, the mentioned khabar is better and correct. Or 'la'l-khabar dhalik' is the answer of the condition, i.e., 'what is mentioned is its khabar.' And if the nominal clause on which hatta enters does not have its khabar mentioned, then it is estimated from the same kind as what precedes, e.g., 'akaltu al-samakata hatta ra'suha' with nominative of 'ra's': this is mubtada, and its khabar is estimated from the same kind as what precedes, i.e., 'hatta ra'suha ma'kul'. And if hatta enters on verbs, it is of three kinds: sometimes for ghaya, and sometimes only for sababiyya, and sometimes for 'ataf, i.e., simply to include the conjuncted with the conjuncted-to without considering ghaya or sababiyya. Then the detail of these three types: if the first part (sadr) admits extension, i.e., what precedes hatta is capable of extension, and the last part (akhir) is capable of being an end, i.e., the first portion can extend and end at the last portion, then hatta here is for ghaya, like 'until they give the jizya' (hatta yu'tu al-jizya): what precedes hatta (fighting) admits extension, and accepting jizya is capable of being its end. Similarly, 'hatta tasta'nisu' (until you seek permission): what precedes hatta (preventing entry into another's house) admits extension, and seeking permission is capable of being its end. And if the first part does not admit extension and the last part is not capable of being an end, then one looks: if it is suitable for the first to be a cause for the second, i.e., if what precedes hatta is capable of being a cause for the action that follows hatta, then hatta is for sababiyya, which indicates causation, because the reward and the caused are intended from the thing, so it is like ghaya. For example, 'I accepted Islam until I enter Paradise' (aslamtu hatta adkhula al-jannata): here the meaning of ghaya is not possible, because if aslamtu means the act of accepting Islam, there is no extension; and if it means steadfastness in Islam, then entering Paradise is not capable of being its end and point of termination; rather, with entering Paradise, Islam becomes firmer and stronger. Therefore here hatta is for sababiyya. And if not, then for 'ataf: i.e., if what precedes hatta cannot be a cause for what follows hatta, then that hatta is purely for 'ataf, not for ghaya nor sababiyya. And for pure 'ataf, the existence of both actions is required so that inclusion is realized, which is required by 'ataf. For example, if he says: 'My slave is free if I do not strike you until you shout' (in lam adribka hatta tasiha): this example is for ghaya, i.e., hatta in 'hatta tasiha' is for ghaya, because the first part of the speech (striking) admits extension, and 'until you shout' is capable of being an end, because the shouting of the struck one usually becomes the end for striking. So in this example, if he stops striking before the struck one shouts, he becomes a violator (hanith); and if he continues striking until the struck one shouts, he does not violate. And if he says: 'My slave is free if I do not come to you until you feed me' (in lam atika hatta tuf'idani): in this example, hatta is for sababiyya, not ghaya, because the last part (feeding) is not capable of being an end for what precedes (coming), but rather it is a motivation for coming, and coming has the potential for causation, and reward can follow it. Therefore it is considered as sababiyya. So if he comes and the addressee did not feed him, he does not violate (la yahnath), because this could only be in the case of ghaya, and here the meaning of ghaya is not possible. And if he says: 'until the food is with you' (hatta al-ghada' 'indaka), i.e., he says 'in lam atika hatta al-ghada' 'indaka', then in this example hatta is purely for 'ataf.
Source pages p. 359

Commentary
This passage is a detailed analysis of the particle 'hatta' (حتى) from the perspective of Hanafi usul al-fiqh, specifically how its different usages affect legal rulings, particularly in oaths. The author (presumably Sadr al-Shariah or a commentator) explains that 'hatta' can function in three ways: as a ghaya (limit/end), as sababiyya (cause), or as 'ataf (conjunction). The distinction is crucial because it determines whether a person who swears an oath violates it or not. For ghaya, the action before 'hatta' must be capable of extension and the action after 'hatta' must be a natural endpoint. For example, in 'I will strike you until you shout,' the shouting is a natural end of striking, so if the striker stops before shouting, he violates his oath; if he continues until shouting, he does not. For sababiyya, the first action causes the second, but the second is not an end; rather it is a motivation. In 'I will come to you until you feed me,' the feeding is the cause for coming, not a limit. So if he comes but is not fed, he does not violate because his oath was contingent on the cause, not the effect. For 'ataf, 'hatta' simply conjoins two actions without implying causality or limit, e.g., 'I will not come to you until the food is with you.' The passage also covers grammatical cases like 'hatta ibtida'iyyah' (independent clause) and provides conditions for each usage, emphasizing that the speaker's mental intention matters. This analysis is essential for Hanafi jurists when interpreting oaths and conditional statements, as the literal meaning of 'hatta' determines the legal consequences.

Key Terms
حتى (hatta): A particle that can indicate limit (ghaya), cause (sababiyya), or conjunction ('ataf), with distinct legal effects on oaths.
غاية (ghaya): A limit or endpoint; the action before hatta extends until the action after hatta is reached.
سببية (sababiyya): Causation; the action before hatta is a cause for the action after hatta, though the latter is not an endpoint.
عطف ('ataf): Conjunction; hatta simply connects two actions without implying limit or cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the phrase 'حتى مطلع الفجر', what function does هatta serve?
A) غاية (limit)
B) سببية (cause)
C) عطف (conjunction)
D) ابتدائية (independent clause)

Key Takeaway
The legal interpretation of the particle هلta depends on whether the preceding action admits extension and whether the following action is a natural end; misclassification changes the ruling in oaths.
