Interpreting the Particle 'الى' in Legal Texts
Explains the particle 'الى' indicating termination and its contextual interpretation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul rule for interpreting the particle 'الى' in legal texts and identify which interpretation (termination, attachment to an implicit, or postponement) applies based on context.

Core Idea
The meaning of 'الى' in legal texts depends on context: it may indicate termination, attach to an implicit, or signal postponement.

This lesson examines how Hanafi usul scholars interpret the particle 'الى' (ilā) when it appears in legal statements. The rule is that if the context can accommodate the primary meaning of termination, then 'الى' is taken in that sense. If not, we search for an implicit word to which it can attach; if that is impossible, it indicates postponement of the action. We will walk through the rule step by step using the examples of a sale contract and a divorce pronouncement, and note the dissenting view of Imam Zufar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the context of the speech
Determine the action or transaction described in the beginning of the speech (صدر الكلام). This sets the framework for interpreting 'الى'.
For example, in 'بعت الی شهر', the speech begins with a sale contract.
2
Check if context accommodates literal termination
Ask whether the action can logically come to an end at the specified point. If yes, 'الى' retains its primary meaning of termination.
In sale, the contract cannot terminate after one month while leaving the price unpaid, so literal termination is ruled out.
3
Look for an implicit word (محذوف) for attachment
If literal termination is impossible, search for a word implied by the context that makes sense with 'الى'. The speech must indicate this implicit word.
In 'بعت الی شهر', the implicit word is 'أجلت' (I deferred), so the meaning becomes 'I sold and I deferred the price for a month'.
4
If no implicit word, consider postponement
If attachment to an implicit is not possible, and the context can accommodate postponement (تأخير) of the action, then 'الى' is interpreted as postponing the action's occurrence.
In 'أنت طالق الى شهر' with no intention of immediacy or postponement, 'الى' indicates that divorce occurs after a month.
5
Note Zufar's dissenting view
Imam Zufar holds that in divorce contexts, the divorce is immediate and the time specification is void, disagreeing with the mainstream Hanafi position.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; the mufta bihi is the mainstream view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(الی) لانتهاء الغاية لفظ غانیہ سے مراد مسافت ہے جیسے کہا جاتا ہے من لابتد الغایہ والى لانتهاء الغايته تو مراد ابتداء المسافة اور انتہا المسافة ہوتا ہے کیونکہ غایتہ کا حقیقی مفہوم نہایتہ ہے۔ نہایت کی نہ ابتدا ہوتی ہے نہ انتہا۔ البتہ چونکہ غایہ معنی نہایتہ جزو مسافہ ہے تو تسمیة الکل باسم الجزء کے طور پر غانیہ سے مراد مسافہ لی جاتی ہے ۔ قصد الکلام ان احتمله فظاهر اگر صدر كلام انتهاء الى الغابية کا احتمال یعنی صلاحیت رکھتا ہے تو فظاهر یعنی پھر ظاہر بات یہی ہے کہ الی اپنے معنی انتہاء الغانیہ پر محمول ہوگا ۔ والا اگر صدر کلام احتمال انتہا الی الغایتہ کا نہیں رکھتا تو پھر دیکھا جائیگا کہ خان امکن تعلقه بمحذوف دل الکلام علیہ اگر الی کا تعلق ایسے محذوف سے ممکن ہے جس پر یہ کلام دال ہو تو فذاك پھر اسی محذوف سے اس کو متعلق کیا جائیگا . نحو بعت الی شعر میں يتأجل الثمن لان صدر الکلام کیونکہ صدر کلام یہاں بیع ہے اس کے اندر انتھا، الی الغایہ کا احتمال نہیں ہوسکتا کیونکہ بیچ ایک ماہ تک رہے پھر ختم ہو جائے ایسے نہیں ہو سکتا لكن يمكن تعلق الخ یعنی الی شہر کا تعلق ایک محذوف سے ممکن ہے جس پر یہ کلام دال ہے وہ ہے اجلت تو تقدیر عبارت یوں ہوگی بعث وأجلت الثمن الى شهر تو تأجيل شمن ہو جائیگی ایک ماہ تک وان لم لیکن اگر کلمہ الی کا تعلق ایسے محذوف کے ساتھ ممکن نہیں جس پر کلام دال ہو تو يحمل على تاخیر صدر الکلام ان احتمله اگر صدر کلام احتمال تاخیر رکھتا ہو تو تاخیر پر محمول کیا جائیگا۔ بحوانت طالق الى شعر الم اور اس کے اندر نہ نیت تنجیز ہوا اور نہ تا خبر تو اس وقت میں الی شر کو ایقاع کی طرف منصرف کیا جائیگا تو گویا ایقاع طلاق بعد از شہر ہو گا۔ عورت فی الحال مطلقہ نہیں ہو گی بلکہ مفتی شہر کے بعد ہوگی ۔ وعند زفرا اور امام زفر کے نزدیک طلاق فی الحال واقع ہو جائیگی اور یہ وصف توقیت لغو ہو جائے گی۔
(Ila) for the end of the limit. The word 'ghāya' means distance, as it is said: 'min li-ibtidā' al-ghāya wa ilā li-intihā' al-ghāya', so what is meant is the beginning of the distance and the end of the distance, because the real meaning of 'ghāya' is 'nihāya' (end). The end has neither a beginning nor an end. However, since 'ghāya' meaning 'nihāya' is part of the distance, by way of naming the whole with the name of a part, 'ghāya' is used to mean the distance. The intention of the speech: if it can accommodate (the end of the limit), then it is apparent (zaahir), i.e., the apparent thing is that 'ilā' is interpreted in its meaning of termination of the limit. Otherwise, if the beginning of the speech does not accommodate the probability of termination by 'ilā', then it is seen whether its attachment to an implicit (mahdhūf) is possible which the speech indicates. If it is possible, then it is attached to that implicit. Example: 'bā'tu ilā shahr' — the price is deferred (yata'ajjal al-thaman) because the beginning of the speech here is sale, and it cannot have the probability of termination by 'ilā', because it is not possible that the sale lasts for a month and then ends. However, its attachment to an implicit is possible, which the speech indicates, and that is 'ajaltu' (I deferred). So the estimated wording is: 'ba'tu wa ajaltu al-thamana ilā shahr', thus the deferment of the price for a month. And if not, i.e., if the attachment of the word 'ilā' to such an implicit is not possible, then it is interpreted as postponement (ta'khīr) of the beginning of the speech, if the beginning of the speech accommodates it. Example: 'anti ṭāliq ilā shahr' — if there is no intention of immediacy (tanjīz) nor postponement, then 'ilā' is directed to occurrence (īqā'), so the occurrence of divorce is after a month. The woman is not divorced immediately, but after a month. And according to Zufar, divorce occurs immediately, and the specification of time becomes void.
Source pages p. 365

Commentary
This passage explains the usul rule for interpreting the particle 'الى' (ilā) when it appears in legal texts. The author first defines 'غاية' (ghāyah) as a distance or limit, clarifying that it is used metaphorically to denote the endpoint. The key principle is that if the context of the speech can reasonably accommodate the meaning of termination (intihā' al-ghāya), then 'ilā' is taken in its primary sense. If not, we look for an implicit word to which 'ilā' can attach. In the example of sale ('bā'tu ilā shahr'), the sale cannot end after a month, so 'ilā' is attached to an implicit verb 'ajaltu' (I deferred), meaning the price is payable after a month. In the divorce example ('anti ṭāliq ilā shahr'), if there is no intention of immediate or postponed divorce, 'ilā' is interpreted as postponement, so divorce occurs after a month. Imam Zufar's contrary view is noted: he considers the divorce immediate and the time specification void.

Key Terms
الى (ila): حرف جر يفيد انتهاء الغاية (a preposition indicating termination of a limit)
غاية (ghaya): المنتهى أو المسافة (the limit or distance)
محذوف (mahdhuf): لفظ مقدر أو محذوف دل عليه الكلام (an implicit word that the speech indicates)

Key Takeaway
When interpreting 'الى' in legal texts, first check if the context allows termination; if not, look for an implicit word or consider postponement; the immediate context determines the meaning.

Inclusion of the Limit in the Ruling
Determining whether the limit (ghāya) is included in the ruling of the limited thing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule to determine whether a stated limit (ghāya) is included in the legal ruling of the limited thing.

Core Idea
The limit is excluded if it was an inherent endpoint; if created by speech, inclusion hinges on whether the initial term encompasses the limit.

In legal texts, phrases like 'to' or 'until' often set a limit. A key question is whether that limit itself falls under the preceding ruling. The Hanafi school provides a nuanced answer: it depends on whether the limit was inherent in reality or imposed by the speaker, and whether the initial term of the ruling naturally covers the limit. This lesson unpacks the rule through classical examples.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of limit
Determine if the limit was an inherent endpoint before the speaker's speech (e.g., natural boundaries like a fish's head) or if it became a limit only because the speaker used the word 'ilā'.
Inherent limits exist objectively; others are linguistic devices.
2
Apply the first scenario: inherent limit
If the limit is inherent, it is NOT included in the ruling. Example: 'I sold the garden from this wall to that wall' – the second wall is not part of the sale.
This holds regardless of whether the initial term encompasses the limit.
3
Apply the second scenario: non-inherent limit
If the limit is not inherent, examine whether the beginning of the speech (e.g., the object noun) encompasses the limit. If it does NOT encompass it, the limit is excluded (e.g., 'complete the fast until night' – night is not part of fasting). If it DOES encompass it, the limit is included (e.g., 'wash your hands up to the elbows' – elbows are part of 'hands').
When encompassed, the limit is mentioned to exclude what lies beyond it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم الغاية ان كانت غاية قبل تکلمہ اس میں اختلاف ہے کہ ما بعد الی ماقبل کے حکم میں داخل ہے یا نہ تو مصنف کے نزدیک جو مختار ہے اس کی تفصیل کرتے ہوئے کہا ثم الغایتہ الخ متکلم کے تکلم کرے سے پہلے اگر وہ غایتہ متقی یعنی قبل ازیں کہ متکلم نے لفظ الی استعمال کر کے اسے غایتہ بنایا وہ فی الواقع اور نفس الامر میں غایتہ تھی ماقبل کے حکم میں داخل نہیں ہوگی جیسے بعث ہذا البستان من بذا الحائط الى ذالك الحائط اور اكلت السمكة الى راسما لا یدخل تحت المغیا یعنی یہ غایتہ مغیا کے حکم میں داخل نہیں ہوگی دور مثالیں دیگر اشارہ کیا کہ صدر کلام خواہ متناول للغاتیہ ہو جیسے سمکہ اور راس یا متناول نہ ہو جیسے بستان و حائط ان دونوں صورتوں میں غایتہ حکم مفیا میں داخل نہیں ہوگی وان لم تکن یعنی متکلم کے تکلم سے پہلے وہ غایہ بطور نفس الامر کے نہیں تھی بلکہ متکلم کے تکلم بابی کی وجہ سے وہ غانیہ ہے۔ فصدر الکلام پھر دیکھا جائیگا کہ اگر صدر کلام اسے متناول نہیں ہے فکذلک تو اس وقت میں بھی غایتہ داخل تحت المغیا نہیں ہوگی فعي لمد الحکم یہ جملہ معترضہ ہے بین الشرط والجزا یعنی ان لم یتنا ولا شرط ہے فکذالک جزا فعی امدالحکم یہ جملہ معترضہ ہے مقصد یہ ہے کہ یہ غایتہ صرف مدحکم کا فائدہ دے گی یعنی حکم کو کھینچ کر غایت تک پہونچائیگی اور فایته خارج از حکم رہیگی نحوا تموا الصيام الی اللیل تو صیام لیل کو متناول نہیں ہے لہذا یہ حکم قیام میں داخل نہیں ہوگی فیحرم الوصال فی الصیام و ان تناول اگر صدر کلام اس غانیہ کو متناول ہے جیسے اید یکم الی المرافق میں لفظ یہ مرفق کو متناول ہے کیونکہ یہ کا اطلاق اصابع سے لیکر مناکب واباط تک ہوتا ہے نذكرها لاسقاط ما ورائها اس وقت ذکر غایہ ماوراء غایتہ کے اسقاط کے لئے ہو گا الی المرافق کا لفظ حکم غسل کو مناکب سے لیکر مرافق تک اسقاط عمل کر دے گا اور مرافق فاغسلوا اید یکم کے حکم میں داخل رہیں گی فتدخل تحت المغیا اسی تحت حكم المغيا وهو الغسل
Then, the limit (ghāyah): if it was a limit before the speaker's speech, there is disagreement whether what comes after 'ilā' is included in the ruling of what comes before. The author's chosen (mukhtār) position is detailed: if the limit was a limit in reality before the speaker's utterance, i.e., before the speaker used the word 'ilā' to make it a limit, it was a limit in actuality and in itself, then it is not included in the ruling of what comes before. Example: 'ba'tu hādhā al-bustān min hādhā al-ḥā'iṭ ilā dhālika al-ḥā'iṭ' and 'akaltu al-samaka ilā ra'sihā' — the limit does not enter under the limited (mighyā). These two examples indicate that whether the beginning of the speech encompasses the limit (like fish and head) or does not encompass it (like garden and wall), in both cases the limit is not included in the ruling of the limited. And if it was not (i.e., the limit was not a limit in reality before speech), but rather it is a limit due to the speaker's speech (by making it a limit), then we look: if the beginning of the speech does not encompass it, then likewise the limit is not included under the limited. This is a parenthetical sentence between the condition and the result, meaning: 'if it does not encompass it' is the condition, and 'so likewise' is the result. This limit only serves to extend the ruling, i.e., it stretches the ruling to the limit, and what is beyond the limit remains outside the ruling. Example: 'atimmū al-ṣiyām ilā al-layl' — the prayer does not encompass the night, so this limit is not included in the ruling of fasting, thus it is forbidden to join (wiṣāl) fasting. And if it (the beginning of the speech) encompasses the limit, like 'aydiyakum ilā al-marāfiq' — the word 'aydī' encompasses the elbows because its application extends from fingers to shoulders and armpits. We mention it to drop what is beyond it. In this case, mentioning the limit (the elbows) is to drop what is beyond it. The phrase 'ilā al-marāfiq' drops the ruling of washing from the shoulders to the elbows, and the elbows remain included in the command 'faghsilū aydiyakum', so they enter under the limited, i.e., under the ruling of the limited, which is washing.
Source pages p. 365

Commentary
This passage discusses the rule regarding whether the limit (ghāyah) indicated by 'الى' is included in the ruling of the limited thing (mighyā). The author distinguishes two scenarios: first, if the limit was inherently a limit in reality before the speaker's speech (e.g., the head of a fish is naturally the end, or the second wall of a garden is its boundary), then the limit is not included in the ruling. For example, selling a garden 'from this wall to that wall' means the second wall is not sold; eating a fish 'up to its head' means the head is not eaten. Second, if the limit is not inherently a limit but is made so by the speaker's speech, then we look at the beginning of the speech: if it does not encompass the limit (like 'complete the fast until night' — the fast does not normally include night), then the limit is not included, so continuous fasting (wiṣāl) is forbidden. If the speech does encompass the limit (like 'wash your hands up to the elbows' — the word 'hand' includes the elbow), then the limit is mentioned to exclude what is beyond, and the limit itself is included in the ruling. Thus, elbows must be washed.

Key Terms
غاية (ghaya): المنتهى (the limit or endpoint)
مغيا (mighya): ما دخل تحت الحكم قبل الغاية (the limited thing, that which is subject to the ruling before the limit)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on the second wall in the sale 'بعت هذا البستان من هذا الحائط إلى ذلك الحائط'?
A) The second wall is included in the sale
B) The second wall is not included in the sale
C) It depends on the price
D) It depends on the type of wall

Key Takeaway
The limit is only excluded if it is an inherent endpoint; otherwise, if the initial term encompasses it, it is included.

The Four Grammatical Opinions on 'Ila' and Their Usul Significance
Presenting the four grammatical schools' views on inclusion/exclusion of the limit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four grammatical madhāhib regarding the particle 'ilā' and apply them to determine whether the limit is included in the ruling, using the Hanafi contextual approach.

Core Idea
The particle 'ilā' can include or exclude the limit; grammarians differ, but Hanafi usul reads it contextually.

In this passage, the author presents the four well-known grammatical opinions on the particle 'ilā'. This is not a mere linguistic exercise: it directly impacts how we interpret the limits in Quranic commands, such as washing the hands up to the elbows in wudu. Understanding these opinions equips you to see how different jurists derived different rulings from the same text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
The particle 'ilā' governs a limit (ghāyah). The question is: does the limit (the object of 'ilā') enter under the ruling of the preceding thing (dukhūl) or not ('adam al-dukhūl)? This is the central grammatical dispute.
The answer affects legal obligations, e.g., whether the elbow must be washed in wudu.
2
List the four opinions
Recall the four madhāhib: (1) Inclusion is real, exclusion is metaphorical. (2) Exclusion is real, inclusion is metaphorical. (3) Sharedness (ishtirāk): both meanings are real. (4) Inclusion if the limit is of the same genus as the limited; otherwise exclusion.
These are abstract views; their concrete application depends on context.
3
Connect to usul al-fiqh
Each opinion leads to a different default ruling when interpreting a text containing 'ilā'. For example, in Quran 5:6, 'wash your hands up to (ilā) the elbows.' Opinion 1 defaults to inclusion (wash elbows), opinion 2 defaults to exclusion (do not wash elbows).
Hanafi usul does not mechanically adopt one grammatical opinion; it considers contextual clues (qarīnah).
4
Apply to a concrete example
Using the wudu example: According to opinion 1, the elbows are washed (included). According to opinion 2, they are not. According to opinion 3, both are possible until context decides. According to opinion 4, elbows are included because they are of the same genus (hands). The Hanafi fatwa includes the elbows, consistent with opinion 1 and 4, based on contextual evidence from prophetic practice.
This demonstrates how grammatical analysis feeds into istinbāṭ.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وللنحويين في الى اربعة مذاهب الی کے متعلق جو مصنف کے نزدیک مختار تھا اس کی تفصیل کر دی یہاں سے اپنے مختار پر دلیل پیش کر رہے ہیں حاصل یہ کہ الی کے متعلق نحویوں کے مذاہب اربعہ ہیں۔ پہلا مذہب ہے۔ الدخول الامجازا یعنی غایتہ حکم مخیا کے تحت داخل ہوگی یہ الی کا حقیقی معنی ہے اور عدم دخول مجاز ہے دعکسہ کا یہ مذہب ثانی ہے الی کا حقیقی مفہوم یہ ہے کہ غایتہ حکم مفیا کے تحت داخل نہیں ہوگی اور دخول فی حکم المغیا یہ مجاز ہے کا لمرافق تو اس مذہب ثانی کے لحاظ دخول مرافق تحت حكم المغياء هو الغسل مجازاً ہوگا حقیقت نہیں. والاشتراک یہ مذہب ثالث ہے یعنی الی دونوں معنی دخول اور عدم دخول میں مشترک ہے اس مذہب ثالث کے لحاظ سے دخول غايته تحت حكم المغیا اور عدم دخول دونوں حقیقی معنی ہوں گے کیونکہ اشتراک میں دونوں معنی موضوع نہ ہوتے ہیں والدخول ان كان ما بعدها من جنس ما قبلها به مذهب رابع ہے حاصل یہ کہ اگر ما بعد الی ماقبل کی جنس سے سے تو ما بعد محکم ما قبل
And for the grammarians, there are four madhāhib regarding 'ilā'. The author has detailed his chosen position regarding 'ilā', and from here he is presenting evidence for his choice. The summary is that there are four madhāhib of grammarians regarding 'ilā'. The first madhhab is: inclusion (al-dukhūl) is metaphorical? (al-majāz), i.e., the limit enters under the ruling of the limited, this is the real meaning of 'ilā', and non-inclusion is metaphorical. Its opposite (wa 'aksuhu) is the second madhhab: the real meaning of 'ilā' is that the limit does not enter under the ruling of the limited, and inclusion in the ruling of the limited is metaphorical. For example, the elbow: according to this second madhhab, the inclusion of the elbow under the ruling of the limited, which is washing, is metaphorical, not real. And the third madhhab is sharedness (al-ishtirāk), i.e., 'ilā' is shared between the two meanings of inclusion and non-inclusion. According to this third madhhab, both inclusion of the limit under the ruling of the limited and non-inclusion are real meanings, because in sharedness, both meanings are lexically assigned (mawḍū'). And the fourth madhhab is: inclusion (al-dukhūl) if what comes after it is of the same genus as what comes before it. The summary is that if what comes after 'ilā' is of the same genus as what comes before, then what comes after is included in the ruling of what comes before.
Source pages p. 366

Commentary
This passage enumerates the four grammatical schools (madhāhib al-nuḥāt) regarding the particle 'الى' and whether it includes its object (the limit) in the ruling of the preceding thing. The first opinion holds that inclusion is the real meaning, and non-inclusion is metaphorical. The second opinion holds the opposite: non-inclusion is real, inclusion is metaphorical. The third opinion holds that 'ilā' is shared (mushtarak) between both meanings, so both are real. The fourth opinion conditions inclusion on the limit being of the same genus as the limited; if so, it is included. The text is presented as part of the author's argument for his chosen view (which was discussed earlier). This provides a grammatical foundation for the usul rules on interpreting 'ilā'.

Key Terms
الى (ila): A preposition (ḥarf jar) with multiple possible meanings regarding inclusion/exclusion of the limit.
مذهب (madhhab): School of thought among grammarians.
دخول (dukhūl): Inclusion of the limit in the ruling.
عدم دخول (adam al-dukhūl): Exclusion of the limit from the ruling.
اشتراك (ishtirāk): Sharedness; a word having multiple real meanings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the third grammatical madhhab (الاشتراك) regarding the particle 'الى', what is the status of inclusion of the limit in the ruling?
A) Inclusion is real, exclusion is figurative
B) Exclusion is real, inclusion is figurative
C) Both inclusion and exclusion are real (literal)
D) Inclusion occurs only if the limit is of the same genus

Key Takeaway
There is no single grammatical rule for 'ilā'; the Hanafi usul method weighs context and usage to determine inclusion or exclusion.

Rulings of Qabl, Ba'd, and 'Ind in Conditional Divorce
Textual analysis of three particles' legal effect

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi linguistic rulings for 'qabl', 'ba'd', and 'ind' to determine the number of divorces in conditional divorce statements.

Core Idea
In conditional divorce, 'before' gives precedence to the described divorce, 'after' reverses it, and 'at' only indicates presence without obligation.

In Hanafi fiqh, the precise wording of a divorce statement determines its legal effect. This lesson examines three key particles: 'qabl' (before), 'ba'd' (after), and 'ind' (at/with). Understanding their linguistic implications is essential for correctly applying the rules of conditional divorce.

Guided Path
1
Identify the particle
Examine the divorce statement to see which particle is used: 'qabl', 'ba'd', or 'ind'. This determines the rule to apply.
2
Determine the effect of 'qabl'
If 'qabl' qualifies a divorce, that divorce occurs first. The other divorce may become void if the wife becomes irrevocably divorced after the first.
3
Determine the effect of 'ba'd'
If 'ba'd' qualifies a divorce, that divorce occurs after the first. It is the opposite of 'qabl'.
4
Apply the rule for 'ind'
If 'ind' is used, it only indicates presence, not obligation. In acknowledgment statements, it confirms possession without liability.
5
Consider the wife's status
Whether the wife is consummated (مدخولہ) or unconsummated (غير مدخولہ) affects the outcome because an unconsummated wife becomes irrevocable after one divorce.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جائیگی اگر مقارنتہ نہ ہوتی تو پھر ایک اولا واقع ہوتی اس کے ساتھ بائنہ ہو جاتی دوسری لغو ہو جاتی کیونکہ اس کے لئے محل باقی نہیں رہا قبل للتقديم لفظ قبل تقدیم کے لئے ہے یعنی جس کی وصف بنے گا وہی مقدم ہوگا۔ اگر غیر مدخولہ کو کہتا ہے انت طالق واحدة قبل واحدة تو غیر مدخولہ کو صرف ایک طلاق واقع ہوگی کیونکہ یہ قبلیتہ اول طلاق جو مذکور ہوتی ہے یہ اسی کی صنعت ہے لہذا وہ مقدماً واقع ہو جائے گی۔ غیر مدخولہ ایک کے ساتھ بائنہ ہو جائے گی ثانی کے لئے وہ محل باقی نہیں ہے اس لئے لغو ہو جائے گی ۔ و ثنتان لو قال قبلها اگر غیر مدخولہ کو یوں کہتا ہے انتِ طالق واحدة قبلها واحدة تو پھر دو طلاق واقع برونگی کیونکہ لفظ طلاق جو اولاً مذکور ہوا ہے وہ تو فی الحال واقع ہو جائے گا ۔ والذی وصف اور وہ طلاق جس کی وصف قبلیتہ کے ساتھ کی ہے وہ اس فی الحال واقع شدہ سے پہلے ہے تو وہ بھی فی الحال واقع ہو جاے گی کیونکہ جب کوئی شخص ایقاع الطلاق فی الماضی کی خبر دے تو وہ فی الحال واقع ہوتی ہے جب یہ دونوں معا دفعة واحدة واقع ہوئیں تو مطلقہ بطلقتین ہو جائے گی ۔ وبعد علی العکس یہ قبل کا الٹ سے اگر عزیز تولہ کو کہہ انت طالق واحدة بعد واحدہ تو دو طلاق واقع ہوں گی وجہ وہ ہے جو قبلها واحدة میں پیش کی گئی ہے اگر غیر مدخولہ کو کہتا ہے انت طالق واحدة بعدها واحدة تو ایک طلاق واقع ہوگی وجہ وہی ہے جو قبل واحدة میں بیان کی گئی ہے ۔ وعند للحضرة لفظ عند حضور کے لئے ہے یعنی اس سے یہ معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ متکلم کے ہاں یہ شنی حاضر ہے لزوم اور وجوب اس میں نہیں ہے ۔ اگر کوئی شخص کہہ لفلان عندی الف تو یہ ودیعہ کا اقرار ہوگا لزوم اور وجوب پر دال نہیں ۔
If there were no simultaneity, then one [divorce] would occur first, with it she becomes irrevocable, and the second becomes void because there is no place left for it. 'Qabl' is for precedence, meaning: the one that is described will be given precedence. If he says to an unconsummated wife: 'You are divorced once before once', then only one divorce occurs, because the precedence is an attribute of the first divorce mentioned; therefore it occurs first. The unconsummated wife becomes irrevocable with one; for the second there is no place left, so it is void. And two [divorces occur] if he says before it: if he says to an unconsummated wife: 'You are divorced once before it once', then two divorces occur, because the word 'divorce' mentioned first will occur immediately. And the one described with precedence before the immediately occurring one also occurs immediately, because when a person reports the effectuation of divorce in the past, it occurs immediately. When these two occur together simultaneously, the woman becomes divorced twice. And 'after' is the opposite of 'before'. If he says to a consummated wife: 'You are divorced once after once', then two divorces occur, the reason is the same as presented in 'before it once'. If he says to an unconsummated wife: 'You are divorced once after once', then one divorce occurs, the reason is the same as explained in 'before once'. And 'when' (عند) is for presence; it indicates that something is present with the speaker; there is no obligation or requirement in it. If a person says: 'So-and-so has something with me' (لفلان عندي الف), it is an acknowledgment of a deposit; it does not indicate obligation.
Source pages p. 370

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis discussing the legal effect of the words 'before' (قبل), 'after' (بعد), and 'at' (عند) in divorce formulas. The author explains that the word 'before' assigns precedence to the divorce it describes, so if a husband says to an unconsummated wife 'You are divorced once before once,' only one divorce occurs because the second would have no effect since the wife becomes irrevocable after the first. However, if he says 'You are divorced once before it once,' two divorces occur because the word 'divorce' itself is mentioned first and takes effect immediately, while the described one also takes effect simultaneously because reporting a past divorce brings it into the present. The same logic applies to 'after' in reverse: for a consummated wife, two divorces occur; for an unconsummated wife, only one. The word 'at' (عند) simply indicates presence and does not create any obligation, as seen in the acknowledgment of a deposit (وديعة) where it merely confirms possession without liability.

Key Terms
قبل (qabl): In this passage, 'qabl' indicates precedence in occurrence of divorce; the divorce described with 'qabl' is given priority.
بعد (ba'd): In this passage, 'ba'd' indicates subsequent occurrence; it works opposite to 'qabl' in divorce statements.
عند (ind): Used to indicate presence of something with the speaker; does not imply obligation or legal requirement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One divorce
B) Two divorces
C) Three divorces
D) No divorce

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school derives the legal effect of divorce particles from their literal linguistic meanings: 'qabl' gives precedence, 'ba'd' reverses it, and 'ind' merely indicates presence without obligation.

Conditional Particles 'In', 'Idha', and 'Mata' in Divorce
Explains the legal effect of conditional particles in divorce contexts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi and Sahibayn positions on the temporal meaning of 'idha' in conditional divorce and apply the correct ruling based on the particle used.

Core Idea
The particle 'idha' can be purely conditional (Imam) or retain temporal meaning (Sahibayn), changing when divorce occurs.

In conditional divorce, the precise meaning of the particle used can determine whether a divorce takes effect immediately, at death, or at the wife's choice. This lesson unpacks the legal implications of three Arabic conditionals—'in', 'idha', and 'mata'—as applied by the Hanafi school. You will see how a grammatical dispute between the Kufi and Basri schools leads to a practical difference in rulings between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three particles and their default meanings
Read the passage and note the core description of each particle: 'in' is purely conditional, 'idha' can be conditional or temporal, and 'mata' is purely temporal.
Focus on the Kufi vs Basri distinction for 'idha'.
2
Apply 'in' to a divorce formula
Consider the example 'In lam utalliquk fa-anti taliq'. Since 'in' is purely conditional, the condition (absence of divorce) is uncertain. Thus divorce occurs at death of one spouse.
This is the default Hanafi ruling for 'in'.
3
Analyze the dispute over 'idha'
The passage presents two views: Imam (Kufi) treats 'idha' as purely conditional; Sahibain (Basri) retain its temporal meaning. Apply each to 'Idha lam utalliquk fa-anti taliq' and see the different outcomes.
Imam: divorce at death; Sahibain: divorce at the slightest silence.
4
Review 'mata' and the agreed case
Note that 'mata' is always temporal, so divorce occurs immediately. Then examine the agreement on 'idha shi'ta' = 'mata shi'ta', where both indicate general time, giving the wife choice at any moment.
This shows that in some contexts the dispute is resolved.
5
Summarize the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: in 'Idha lam utalliquk', Imam delays divorce to death; Sahibain make it immediate upon any moment of silence. This affects inheritance rights if death occurs.
Also note the impact on the wife's ability to divorce herself.

نان قال ان لم اطلقك فانت طالق تو اس مقام پر شرط عدم طلاق ہے اور جب تک زوجین زندہ ہیں ممکن الوقوع اور متردد الوجود ہے لہذا عورت فی الحال مطلقہ نہیں ہوگی اور یہ طلاق احد الزوجین کی موت کے وقت واقع ہوگی کیونکہ بعد موت احد الزوجين وقوع طلاق نہیں ہو سکتا لہذا موت تک انتظار کی جائے گی جب موت آنے لگی تو اب ان لم اطلقک کی شرط پوری ہو چکی ہے تو عورت مطلقہ ہو جائیگی۔ جب عورت موت زوج کے وقت مطلقہ ہو رہی ہے اگر غیر مدخولہ ہے تو پھر مستحق میراث نہیں ہوگی اگر

زمان ہوا جیسے اذا حاس الحيس بدلی جناب یعنی جس وقت میں بنائی جاتی ہے تو اس وقت جندب کو بلایا جاتا ہے جیس بنائی جاتی ہے تمر۔ گھی ۔ اقسط یعنی پنیر مایہ سے ان کو خلط ملط کر دیا جاتا ہے یہ میس ہو جاتی ہے ۔ اس شعر کا پہلا حصہ ہے اذا تکون کر بہتہ ادھی لہا یعنی بوقت کر یہ امر کے خواہ حرب ہو یا کوئی اور تکلیف دہ امر تو اس وقت مجھے بلایا جاتا ہے یہ اذا ظرفیہ ہے اور اذا تصبک خصاصة فتجمل یہ اذا برائے شرط ہے شرط کے لئے ہو تو معنی ظرفیہ ساقط ہو جائیگا دعوله في امر كائن الى متحقق فی الحال کمانی قولہ اذا کون کر یہ انکی الہادی عند نزول حادثه او منتظر لا محاله یعنی اذا کی استعمال امر منتظر میں ہوتی ہے جس کا وقوع مستقبل میں ہو گا بشرطیکہ وقوع لا محالہ ہو یعنی وقوع اس کا یعینی اور قطعی ہو جیسے اذ السماء انفطرت ومتى للظرف خاصة كلمہ متی کی وضع صرف معنی ظرفیت کے لئے ہے اس کی استعمال صرف شرط کے لئے نہیں ہوتی جیسے ان کی صرف شرط کے لئے ہوتی تھی اور منی سے معنی ظرفیہ ساقط بھی نہیں ہو سکتا جیسے اذا سے ساقط ہو جاتا تھا علی رأی الکوفی بین اگر بیوی سے کہتا ہے منتی لم اطلقت انت طالق فيقع بادنى سکوت معمولی سکوت کے ساتھ طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی کیونکہ ایسا وقت موجود و چکا ہے جس میں اس نے طلاق نہیں دی اگر چہ قلیل ہی سہی دان قال اذا یعنی جب بیوی کو کہتا ہے اذا لم اطلقک فانت طالق تو صاحبین کے نزدیک یہ متی کی مانند ہے کہ ادنی اسکوت کے ساتھ طلاق واقع ہو جائیگی کیونکہ صاحبین کے نزدیک اذا سے ظرفیتہ ساقط نہیں ہوتی کما ھو من سب البحرين تو صاحبین کے نزدیک کمرہ اذا مثل متنی کے ہے اور امام کے نزدیک لفظ اذا محض شرط کے لئے بھی آتا ہے اور ظرفیہ اس سے ساقط ہو جاتی ہے۔ کما ھو مذہب الكوفيين كما فى اذا شئت فانه کمتی شئت یہ مسئلہ بالاتفاق ہے حاصل اس کا یہ ہے کہ اگر کوئی شخص بیوی سے کہتا ہے طلقی نفسک اداشت یہ بالکل ایسا ہے جیسے کہتا متی شتت یہ دونوں بمعنی ظرف کے ہیں جو عموم اوقات کا فائدہ دیتے ہیں لہذا یہ اختیار مجلس کے ساتھ متقید نہیں ہو گا بلکہ عورت جس وقت چاہے اپنے آپ کو طلاق دے سکتی ہے۔
Conditional words: The word 'in' (if) is purely for condition, and it applies to matters that are at risk of existence (i.e., possibly existing or not). It does not apply to matters that are certain to exist or certain not to exist, unless they are treated as uncertain for some reason. If someone says: 'If I do not divorce you, you are divorced,' then the condition is the absence of divorce, and as long as both spouses are alive, it is possible and uncertain, so the woman is not immediately divorced; the divorce will occur at the time of death of one of the spouses because after death divorce cannot occur. So we wait until death; when death approaches, the condition 'if I did not divorce you' is fulfilled, and she becomes divorced. When she becomes divorced at the time of the husband's death, if she is unconsummated, she will not inherit; if consummated, she will inherit because this is a divorce of death (talaq al-farr). And 'idha' according to the Kufis is for time (zarf) and also for condition, meaning that it is used for the time of occurrence of the thing added to it, so it is a time adverb, like in the verse 'idha hasa al-hais' etc... And 'mata' is purely for time; its usage is not solely for condition like 'in' is solely for condition. And the meaning of time cannot be dropped from 'mata' as it is dropped from 'idha' according to Kufis. If a man says to his wife: 'Mata lam utalliquk fa-anti taliq' (Whenever I do not divorce you, you are divorced), divorce occurs at the slightest silence, because that time has occurred when he did not divorce. And if he says 'Idha lam utalliquk fa-anti taliq' (When I do not divorce you, you are divorced), according to the Sahibain (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is like 'mata', so divorce occurs at the slightest silence, because according to them the time meaning is not dropped from 'idha'. But according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the word 'idha' can be purely for condition, and the time meaning is dropped. As in the case of 'idha shi'ta' (whenever you wish) and 'mata shi'ta' (whenever you wish) are agreed upon; the conclusion is that if a man says to his wife 'Tallaqi nafsaki idha shi'ti' (Divorce yourself whenever you wish), it is exactly like saying 'Mata shi'ti'; both indicate general time, so they are not restricted to the session, and the woman can divorce herself whenever she wishes.
Source pages p. 370

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of conditional particles used in divorce. It first discusses 'in' (if), emphasizing that it applies only to uncertain matters (امر متردد). This has practical application: if a husband says 'If I do not divorce you, you are divorced,' the condition (the absence of divorce) is uncertain as long as both are alive. The divorce only takes effect at death (talaq al-farr), and inheritance depends on consummation. Then the passage moves to 'idha' and 'mata'. It presents the Kufi grammatical view that 'idha' can function both as a time adverb and a conditional particle. The Basri view holds that its primary meaning is time, even when used conditionally. This grammatical dispute has fiqh consequences: According to the Sahibain (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), 'idha' retains its time meaning, so if a husband says 'Idha lam utalliquk fa-anti taliq,' divorce occurs at the slightest silence (because a moment of time has passed without divorce). According to Imam Abu Hanifa, 'idha' is purely conditional like 'in', so the divorce would only occur at death (like the case with 'in'). The passage also notes that 'mata' is purely for time; it never loses its temporal sense. Finally, it presents an agreed case: 'idha shi'ta' and 'mata shi'ta' are synonymous in giving the wife the choice to divorce herself at any time, not just in the session.

Key Terms
ان (in): Conditional particle 'if'; applies only to uncertain matters (متردد الوجود).
اذا (idha): Can be a time adverb (ظرف) or conditional particle; meaning depends on school: Kufi/Hanafi allows dropping time meaning, Basri/Sahibain retain time.
متى (mata): Purely a time adverb; never loses its temporal meaning even when used for condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if a husband says to his wife 'Idha lam utalliquk fa-anti taliq' (When I do not divorce you, you are divorced), when does the divorce occur?
A) Immediately at the slightest silence
B) At the death of one of the spouses
C) After three months
D) It never occurs

Key Takeaway
The particle 'idha' can be interpreted as purely conditional (Imam) or temporal (Sahibain), leading to different timings for conditional divorce.

Resolving Ambiguity of 'Idha' in Conditional Clauses
Interpretation of 'idha' in conditional divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle of doubt (shakk) to resolve ambiguity in conditional divorce clauses like 'idha lam utallik'.

Core Idea
When 'idha' is ambiguous, doubt prevents immediate legal effects; certainty is required for occurrence.

This passage examines a core Hanafi usul tool: how to resolve linguistic ambiguity when a word has multiple possible meanings. The dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), centers on whether 'idha' in conditional divorce means 'if' or 'when'. Understanding their reasoning—especially the role of doubt (shakk)—is essential for grasping Hanafi legal interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ambiguous term
Recognize that 'idha' (إذا) can mean either 'if' (in, إن) as a conditional particle or 'when' (mata, متى) as a temporal adverb.
This ambiguity is the root of the dispute.
2
Analyze the two contexts
Compare 'idha lam utallik' (إذا لم أطلقك) and 'idha shi'ta' (إذا شئت). In the latter, 'idha' is understood as 'when' by consensus. In the former, the Sahibayn also treat it as 'when', but Abu Hanifa treats it as 'if'.
Abu Hanifa must distinguish the two contexts.
3
Apply the doubt principle
In 'idha lam utallik', if 'idha' means 'when', divorce occurs immediately; if it means 'if', divorce occurs at death. This doubt prevents immediate occurrence. In 'idha shi'ta', the divorce is already tied to the woman's will; doubt about termination of that tie prevents termination.
The principle: doubt (shakk) blocks a legal effect that would otherwise be uncertain.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
یہ مسئلہ بالاتفاق ہے بخلاف طلقی نفسک ان شئت یہ متقید بالمجلس ہو گا یعنی جس مجلس میں اختیار دیا ہے اسی مجلس میں عورت اپنے آپ کو طلاق دے سکتی ہے جب اس مجلس سے اٹھ کھڑی ہوئی تو پھر طلاق نہیں دے سکتی تو صاحبین نے کلمہ اذا کو اذالم اطلقک میں کلمہ متی پر محمول کیا ہے جیسے اذا شئت میں بالاتفاق مستی پر محمول تھا۔ وعند ابي حنيفة امام کے نزدیک اذالم اطلقک میں کلمہ اذا لفظ ان پر محمول ہے یعنی اس کا حکم وہی ہے جو ان لم اطلقك فانت طالق کا ہے ۔
فلحتاج البوحنيفة الى الفرق اب امام" کے مذہب پر ضرورت پیش آتی ہے کہ فرق پیش کیا جائے کہ اذالم اطلقک میں اذا بمعنی ان ہے اور سمیعنی متی نہیں اور اذا شئت میں اس کا عکس ہے تو فرمایا والفرق خلاصہ یہ ہے انه لما جاء یعنی جب کلمہ اذا دونوں معنیین کے لئے آتا ہے یعنی ہمعنی ان شرط اور بمعنى متى ظرفيه وقع الشك في مسألتنا في الوقوع في الحال اس مسئلہ سے مراد اذا لم اطلقک ہے یعنی اس قول میں اگر کلمہ اذا کو متی پر محمول کریں تو وقوع طلاق فی الحال ہو جائیں گا اور اگر ان پر محمول کریں تو پھر طلاق بوقت موت کے ہوگی تو وقوع فی الحال میں شک واقع ہو گیا لہذا شک کی بنا پر طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی۔ رحمه في انقطاع تعلقه بالمشية اس دوسرے مسئلہ میں یعنی اذا شئت میں تعلق بالمشیتہ کے انقطاع ہیں شک واقع ہے لہذا شک کی بنا پر منقطع نہیں ہو گا خلاصہ یہ کہ طلقی نفسک اذا شئت میں طلاق فی الحال متعلق بمشيئة المرأة ہو چکی ہے اگر اذا کو محمول ان پر کریں تو تعلق بالمشيته بعد المجلس منقطع ہونا چاہئے اور اگر متی پر محمول کیا جائے تو پھر تعلق بالمشیتہ منقطع نہیں ہو گا۔ اب تعلق بالمشیتہ جو فی الحال ثابت ہو چکا ہے شک کی بنیاد پر منقطع نہیں ہوگا۔
This ruling is by consensus, contrary to 'Divorce yourself if you wish' which is restricted to the session: meaning in the session where authority was given, the woman can give herself divorce only in that session; when she leaves that session, she cannot give divorce. So the Sahibayn interpreted the word 'idha' in 'idha lam utallik' as meaning 'when' (mata), just as in 'idha shi'ta' it is by consensus interpreted as 'when' (mata). According to Abu Hanifa, the Imam, in 'idha lam utallik' the word 'idha' is interpreted as 'if' (in), meaning its ruling is the same as 'in lam utallik fa-ant taliq'. So Abu Hanifa needed to differentiate that in 'idha lam utallik' 'idha' means 'if' and not 'when', and in 'idha shi'ta' it is the opposite. So he said the summary of the difference is: when the word 'idha' comes for both meanings, i.e., meaning 'if' as a conditional particle and meaning 'when' as a temporal adverb, doubt arises in our issue regarding occurrence in the present. The issue meant is 'idha lam utallik': if we interpret 'idha' as 'when', then the divorce occurs immediately; if we interpret it as 'if', then the divorce occurs at the time of death. So doubt occurred regarding immediate occurrence, therefore due to doubt divorce does not occur. In the second issue, i.e., 'idha shi'ta', doubt occurs regarding the termination of attachment to the will, so due to doubt it is not terminated. The summary is that in 'talliqi nafsaki idha shi'ta', the divorce in the present is already attached to the woman's will. If 'idha' is interpreted as 'if', then the attachment to the will should be terminated after the session; if interpreted as 'when', then the attachment to the will is not terminated. Now the attachment to the will which is already established in the present will not be terminated due to doubt.
Source pages p. 372

Commentary
This passage discusses a key usul al-fiqh issue: the interpretation of the word 'idha' in conditional divorce and emancipation. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that 'idha' in 'idha lam utallik' means 'when' (mata), leading to immediate divorce if the condition is not fulfilled by a certain time, while Abu Hanifa holds that it means 'if' (in), so divorce only occurs at death if the husband never divorces. The author explains that Abu Hanifa needed to distinguish this from the phrase 'idha shi'ta' where 'idha' is agreed to mean 'when'. His distinction is based on the principle of doubt (shakk): in 'idha lam utallik', interpreting 'idha' either way leads to different timings of divorce, so doubt prevents its occurrence; in 'idha shi'ta', the divorce is already tied to the woman's will, and doubt prevents termination of that tie. This illustrates the Hanafi method of resolving linguistic ambiguity by preferring the interpretation that avoids uncertainty in legal consequences.

Key Terms
اذا (idha): A word that can mean either 'if' (in) or 'when' (mata), leading to ambiguity in conditional clauses.
شك (shakk): Doubt or uncertainty about the occurrence of a legal effect; used in usul to prevent rulings when certainty is lacking.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Divorce occurs at the husband's death if he never divorces her.
C) Divorce occurs only if the wife asks for it.
D) Divorce is not valid.

Key Takeaway
The interpretation of ambiguous terms in conditional clauses depends on the principle of avoiding doubt (shakk), a core Hanafi usul tool.

The Meaning of 'Kayfa' in Conditional Emancipation and Divorce
Explains that 'kayfa' in 'anta hurr kayfa shi'ta' becomes metaphorical for any quality

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the metaphorical usage of 'kayfa' in conditional divorce/emancipation phrases and apply the Hanafi usul principle that distinguishes between sensory and non-sensory matters to resolve the sahih/main dispute.

Core Idea
In 'anti taliq kayfa shi'ta', 'kayfa' becomes a metaphor delegating the quality of divorce, not the original act.

This lesson examines how the word 'kayfa' (how) functions in the conditional phrases 'anta hurr kayfa shi'ta' and 'anti taliq kayfa shi'ta'. While originally an interrogative about state, in these contexts it takes on a metaphorical meaning of 'with any quality'. Understanding this transformation is key to resolving the dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn over whether the delegation extends to the original divorce or only its quality.

Guided Path
1
Identify the original usage of 'kayfa'
Recognize that 'kayfa' is originally an interrogative asking about the state (hal). Determine if such a question is correct in the context (istiqamah).
If the state can vary, the interrogative is valid; otherwise it becomes void.
2
Distinguish between emancipation and divorce contexts
Slavery has no varying states, so 'kayfa' is void in emancipation, leading to immediate freedom. Divorce has multiple types (raj'i, bain, etc.), so the interrogative can be interpreted metaphorically.
This distinction is crucial for understanding the different rulings.
3
Explain the metaphorical shift
When a literal interrogative is impossible, 'kayfa' becomes a metaphor meaning 'with any quality'. This delegates the choice of quality to the wife in divorce.
The metaphor is derived from the relative pronoun 'ummati' (whatever).
4
Analyze the dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn
Abu Hanifa holds that the original divorce is from the husband, so only the quality is delegated. The Sahibayn argue that in non-sensory matters, state and original are equal, so both are delegated.
The conflict of intentions leads to cancellation and default raj'i under Abu Hanifa; under Sahibayn, the wife can prevent the divorce.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The text presents the default raj'i as the operative ruling, indicating that Abu Hanifa's view is relied upon in practice.
This is the position for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

کیفیات نہیں ہوا کرتیں لبدا عتق میں کیفیتہ کا تعلق صدر کلام سے مستقیم نہیں ہو سکتا لہذا یہاں لفظ کیف باطل ہو جائیں گے عتق واقع ہو جائے گا اور انت طالق کیف شئت طلاق تو واقع ہو جائے گی البتہ تعیین کیفتہ نیست خاوند کی نیست سے مختلف ہے فلا بد من اعتبار النبیت بین تو دونوں نیتین کا اعتبار کرنا ضروری ہے کیونکہ عورت کی طرف خاوند نے خود تغویض کیا ہے اس لئے اس کا اعتبار ضروری ہے دامانیتہ اور نیست روج کا اعتبار اس لئے ضروری ہے کہ ایقاع طلاق میں اصل تو خاوند ہے اس لئے اس کی رائے کا اعتبار چاہئے فاذا تعارضا تساقطا فبقی اصل اب وہی اصل طلاق انت طالق باقی ہے اور یہی رجعی ہے۔ اس لئے رجعی واقع ہو جائیگی وعندهما يتعلق الاصل ايضا صاحبین کے نزدیک جیسے کیفیتہ طلاق رائے مرآۃ کی طرف مفوض ہے اسی طرح خود اصل طلاق بھی اس کی رائے کی طرف مفوض ہے اگر وہ خود طلاق نہ چاہیے تو انت طالق کیف شئت کے ساتھ خود اصل طلاق بھی واقع نہیں ہوگی۔ فعندهما ما لا يقبل الاشارة الحسية صاحبین کے نزدیک ضابطہ یہ ہے کہ جو شئی اشارہ حسیبہ کو قبول نہیں کرتی یعنی جو محسوسات میں سے نہیں ہے جیسے تصرفات شرعیہ طلاق وعتاق و نکاح و غیره فحاله واصله سواء یعنی اس کا حال اور اصل برابر ہیں جیسے یہاں طلاق اصل ہے اور رجعی یا بائنہ ہونا اس کا حال ہے یہ دونوں برابر درجہ کے ہیں ایک متبوع اور اصل دوسرے کو تابع اور فرع اور ایک کو مقدم دوسرے کو مؤخر قرار نہیں دیا جا سکتا لہذا ان کا وجود معاً ہو گا اب جیسے کیف شئت میں حالتہ طلاق مفوض الى رأسى المراۃ ہے اسی طرح خود اصل طلاق بھی اسی کی طرف مفوض ہوگی کیونکہ دونوں کا وجود معاً ہے ۔ اظن ان هذا مبنى الخ مصنف کے حسب خیال اس مسئلہ کی بنیاد صاحبین کے نزدیک یہ ہے کہ
And 'kayfa': its original usage is for asking about the state. So if in the expression where 'kayfa' is used, asking about the state is correct and valid, then—'in istaqama' (if it is correct) the answer is omitted; the author said the answer is 'in' which is omitted. So it is correct to interpret it as a question. Then if asking about the state is not correct and valid, then the word 'kayfa' itself becomes invalid, and the speaker is truthful in his speech, meaning the meaning of his speech is established. So in 'anta hurr kayfa shi'ta', asking about the state is not correct because slavery does not have different states; therefore the slave becomes free immediately with 'anta hurr', and 'kayfa' which was for asking about the state becomes invalid. Know that the word 'kayfa' in the statement 'anta hurr kayfa shi'ta' and 'anti taliq kayfa shi'ta' is not for asking about the state; rather it has become a metaphor, coming from the word 'ummati' which is a relative pronoun, and its meaning metaphorically is 'you are free, you are divorced with whatever quality you wish'. So in this case, the meaning of 'istiqamah' (correctness) is that the connection of the quality (kayfiyyah) to the main clause is correct. In 'anti taliq kayfa shi'ta', it is correct because divorce has different qualities: raj'i, bain, mughallazah. But in slavery, such qualities do not occur. Therefore in emancipation, the connection of the quality to the main clause is not correct, so here the word 'kayfa' becomes invalid and emancipation occurs. And in 'anti taliq kayfa shi'ta', divorce occurs, but the specification of the quality—whether raj'i, bain, light, or severe—remains delegated to the woman's opinion. If the husband has no intention, then the determination of the quality is left to the woman's opinion; whatever she wishes, it will be. If the husband intended a specific quality, and if the woman's intention agrees, then what both intended occurs. If they differ, then it is necessary to consider both intentions, because the husband himself delegated to the woman, so her intention must be considered, and the husband's intention must be considered because the original agent of divorce is the husband. So when they conflict, they cancel out, and the original divorce (anti taliq) remains, which is raj'i. So raj'i divorce occurs. According to them (the Sahibayn), the original also depends (on the wife's will). According to the Sahibayn, just as the quality of divorce is delegated to the woman's opinion, similarly the original divorce itself is delegated to her opinion; if she does not want divorce, then with 'anti taliq kayfa shi'ta' the original divorce does not occur. According to them, the principle is: that which does not accept sensory indication, i.e., is not among sensory things like shar'i transactions (divorce, emancipation, marriage, etc.), its state and its original are equal. For example, here divorce is the original and being raj'i or bain is its state; both are of equal degree; one cannot be considered primary and the other subordinate, or one advanced and the other delayed. So their existence is simultaneous. Now, just as in 'kayfa shi'ta' the state of divorce is delegated to the woman's opinion, similarly the original divorce itself is delegated to her opinion, because both exist simultaneously. The author thinks the basis of this issue according to the Sahibayn is that...
Source pages p. 372

Commentary
This passage analyzes the word 'kayfa' (how) in conditional divorce and emancipation phrases. In Hanafi usul, 'kayfa' is originally an interrogative asking about the state (hal). However, in phrases like 'anta hurr kayfa shi'ta' and 'anti taliq kayfa shi'ta', it takes on a metaphorical meaning equivalent to 'with any quality you wish'. The commentator explains that if 'kayfa' can be correctly interpreted as a question about a variable state, it is retained; otherwise it becomes void. In emancipation, since a slave's state does not vary (freedom is absolute), the question is invalid, so 'kayfa' becomes void and immediate emancipation occurs. In divorce, since divorce has various types (raj'i, bain, etc.), the quality can be specified, so 'kayfa' is a valid delegation of the choice of quality to the wife. The author then addresses the scenario when both husband and wife have intentions for the quality: if they agree, that quality applies; if they disagree, both intentions cancel out and the default raj'i divorce applies. The Sahibayn hold that not only the quality but also the original divorce is delegated to the wife's will, based on the principle that in shar'i transactions that are not sensory, the state and the original are equal; hence the wife's choice extends to the existence of the divorce itself.

Key Terms
كيف (kayfa): Originally a question about state (hal); in these contexts it becomes a metaphor meaning 'with any quality'.
استقام (istaqama): Refers to the correctness of the question about the state; if the verb's state can vary, it is correct to interpret 'kayfa' as an interrogative.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a man says to his wife 'anti taliq kayfa shi'ta' and the husband intends a bain divorce while the wife intends a raj'i divorce, what is the ruling according to Abu Hanifa?
A) The divorce does not occur because of conflicting intentions.
B) A bain divorce occurs because the husband is the original agent.
C) A raj'i divorce occurs because the conflicting intentions cancel out and the default is raj'i.
D) The wife's intention prevails because she was given the choice.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, 'kayfa' in conditional divorce phrases delegates only the quality of divorce; if intentions conflict, the default raj'i applies.

Ruling for Kinayah Words: The Usul of Probability
Explaining the ruling for kinayah divorce words and the usul reasoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to derive the Hanafi ruling for kinayah divorce words using the usul principle of ihtimal (probability) and identify the resulting type of talaq.

Core Idea
Kinayah words require intention; if intended, talaq raj'i occurs unless the word explicitly indicates baynunah.

In this passage, the author examines the kinayah words 'i'taddi' (count your 'iddah) and 'ista'bari' (wait for purity). The ruling is talaq raj'i, not ba'in. The usul reasoning hinges on the probability that these words imply 'iddah, which only occurs after divorce, thus necessarily indicating divorce. We will unpack this derivation step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the kinayah words
Locate the words 'i'taddi' and 'ista'bari' in the passage. These are allusive words that do not directly say 'talaq'.
2
Analyze the literal meaning and probable implications
Consider the literal meaning: 'i'taddi' means 'count' (the menstrual cycles). This implies 'iddah, which only exists after divorce. So the word carries a probability of meaning divorce by necessity.
This probability (ihtimal) is the basis for the Hanafi ruling.
3
Apply the Hanafi usul rule for kinayah
The Hanafi rule: if a kinayah word carries a probability that necessarily leads to divorce, and the speaker intends divorce, then talaq occurs as raj'i (revocable) unless the word explicitly indicates irretrievable separation (baynunah).
Here, the words do not indicate baynunah, so the talaq is raj'i.
4
Note the exception for before consummation
The passage distinguishes between after and before consummation. For pre-consumption, the words still effect talaq but via a different mechanism (majaz) because there is no 'iddah.
This will be covered in the next lesson on the majaz argument.

If the speaker intends transition to divorce, then this divorce will occur upon the description of separation (baynunah) in accordance with the real meaning of the word 'ba'in. Because he intended divorce by it... The word 'i'taddi' is an exception: divorce with the word 'i'taddi' will not be ba'in but will be raj'i. Because it carries the probability of counting... If after consummation... if before consummation... it is established by way of applying the name of the effect to the cause... An objection is raised... The answer is that the necessary condition for applying the effect to the cause is that the effect has specific connection with the cause, and here it does... Similarly 'ista'bari'... also one of the kinayah words, but talaq raj'i will occur... Similarly 'anti wahida' (you are one) is kinayah, and with it talaq raj'i will occur because it does not indicate baynunah.
Source pages p. 376

Commentary
This passage discusses the fiqh ruling of kinayah (allusive) words for divorce. The author explains that for words like 'i'taddi' (count your 'iddah) and 'ista'bari' (wait for purity), if the husband intends divorce, talaq raj'i occurs, not talaq ba'in. The reasoning is based on the probability of meaning: these words can be interpreted as commands related to 'iddah, which necessarily implies divorce. The author addresses the objection that in majaz (metaphor) of applying the effect to the cause, the effect must be the intended purpose of the cause; here 'iddah is not the primary purpose of divorce. The answer is that 'iddah is specifically connected to divorce primarily, so the majaz is valid. For the phrase 'anti wahida' (you are one), similarly talaq raj'i occurs because it does not explicitly indicate separation.

Key Terms
کنایہ (kinayah): An allusive word that may mean divorce but requires intention for the divorce to occur.
اطلاق المسبب على السبب (itlaq al-musabbab 'ala al-sabab): Using the name of the effect (mussabbab) for the cause (sabab) as a type of majaz.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because it means 'divorce' directly
B) Because it implies 'iddah which necessitates divorce
C) Because it is an explicit command
D) Because it indicates baynunah

Key Takeaway
Kinayah words effect talaq raj'i when intended if they carry a probability that necessitates divorce.

The Majaz Argument: Itlaq al-Musabbab 'ala al-Sabab in Kinayah Talaq
Analyzing the objection and response regarding the majaz for kinayah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Hanafi use of itlaq al-musabbab 'ala al-sabab as a valid majaz to justify talaq via kinayah words before consummation.

Core Idea
Itlaq al-musabbab 'ala al-sabab is valid if the effect is specifically connected to the cause, even if not the primary purpose.

In this passage, the author anticipates an objection: the majaz of applying the effect ('iddah) to the cause (divorce) is only valid if the effect is the intended purpose of the cause. Since 'iddah is not the primary purpose of divorce (which is to end the marriage), the objection claims the majaz is invalid. The Hanafi response is that specific connection (ikhtisas) is sufficient. We will analyze this objection and response.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
The objection states that the majaz itlaq al-musabbab 'ala al-sabab requires the effect to be the intended goal (maqsud) of the cause. Here, 'iddah is not the intended goal of divorce; divorce is meant to end the marriage, not to observe 'iddah.
The objector claims the condition is not met.
2
Examine the Hanafi condition for this majaz
The Hanafi response redefines the condition: the effect must be specifically connected (mukhtass) to the cause, not necessarily the primary purpose.
Specific connection means the effect is exclusively or primarily tied to that cause.
3
Apply the condition to 'iddah and divorce
'Iddah is specifically connected to divorce primarily (asala), even though it may also occur in other situations (like death) as secondary. Therefore, the connection is strong enough for valid majaz.
4
Confirm the ruling for pre-consummation cases
For a wife before consummation, there is no 'iddah literally, but the word 'i'taddi' can still indicate divorce through this majaz: the word primarily means 'count your 'iddah', which is metaphorically applied to 'divorce' because 'iddah is the effect of divorce.

Source Text

ہو جائیں گے۔ وكذا انت واحدة یعنی یہ کنایہ ہے اور اس کے ساتھ بھی طلاق رجعی واقع ہوگی کیونکہ اس لفظ میں احتمال طلاق ہے جب خاوند نیت طلاق کرے گا تو اس کے ساتھ ایک رجعیہ واقع ہوگی بائنہ نہیں ہوگی کیونکہ بینونتہ پر یہ لفظ دلالت نہیں کرتا ۔
If the speaker intends transition to divorce, then this divorce will occur upon the description of separation (baynunah) in accordance with the real meaning of the word 'ba'in. Because he intended divorce by it... The word 'i'taddi' is an exception: divorce with the word 'i'taddi' will not be ba'in but will be raj'i. Because it carries the probability of counting... If after consummation... if before consummation... it is established by way of applying the name of the effect to the cause... An objection is raised... The answer is that the necessary condition for applying the effect to the cause is that the effect has specific connection with the cause, and here it does... Similarly 'ista'bari'... also one of the kinayah words, but talaq raj'i will occur... Similarly 'anti wahida' (you are one) is kinayah, and with it talaq raj'i will occur because it does not indicate baynunah.
Source pages p. 376

Commentary
This passage discusses the fiqh ruling of kinayah (allusive) words for divorce. The author explains that for words like 'i'taddi' (count your 'iddah) and 'ista'bari' (wait for purity), if the husband intends divorce, talaq raj'i occurs, not talaq ba'in. The reasoning is based on the probability of meaning: these words can be interpreted as commands related to 'iddah, which necessarily implies divorce. The author addresses the objection that in majaz (metaphor) of applying the effect to the cause, the effect must be the intended purpose of the cause; here 'iddah is not the primary purpose of divorce. The answer is that 'iddah is specifically connected to divorce primarily, so the majaz is valid. For the phrase 'anti wahida' (you are one), similarly talaq raj'i occurs because it does not explicitly indicate separation.

Key Terms
کنایہ (kinayah): An allusive word that may mean divorce but requires intention for the divorce to occur.
اطلاق المسبب على السبب (itlaq al-musabbab 'ala al-sabab): Using the name of the effect (mussabbab) for the cause (sabab) as a type of majaz.
اختصاص (ikhtisas): Specific connection or exclusivity between the effect and the cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the key condition for the validity of itlaq al-musabbab 'ala al-sabab?
A) The effect must be the primary purpose of the cause
B) The effect must be specifically connected to the cause
C) The cause must be a verb
D) The effect must be immediate

Key Takeaway
Specific connection, not primary purpose, is the condition for itlaq al-musabbab 'ala al-sabab.

Dhalalat al-Nas: Status and Application
Hanafi rule on dhalalat al-nas: its proof value and limits

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of dhalalat al-nas, explain its equivalence to ibarah and isharah, and apply the rule that it yields only at contradiction and does not establish hudud or qisas.

Core Idea
Dhalalat al-nas equals ibarah and isharah in proof but yields at conflict and is above qiyas.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, textual indications are ranked. This passage introduces dhalalat al-nas, a ruling derived from the understood meaning of the text. You will learn how it compares to explicit wording (ibarah) and implied meaning (isharah), its superiority over qiyas, and its limitation for penal matters averted by doubts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three textual indications
List ibarat al-nas, isharat al-nas, and dhalalat al-nas. Note how each derives a ruling: from explicit wording, from implication, and from the understood meaning.
This classification is central to Hanafi istinbat.
2
Establish the default equality in proof
The passage states that a ruling proven by dhalalat al-nas is equivalent in proof and definitiveness to one proven by ibarah or isharah. Understand that this is the default rule.
Equality holds unless there is a contradiction (ta'arud).
3
Recognize the exception at contradiction
When ibarah or isharah contradicts dhalalah, they take priority. When ibarah and isharah contradict, ibarah is preferred due to the flow of speech (sawq al-kalam).
This hierarchy resolves conflicts.
4
Compare dhalalah to qiyas and khabar wahid
Dhalalah is superior to qiyas because its meaning is perceived linguistically (from the text itself), while qiyas derives its 'illa by inference. It is also above khabar wahid.
This shows the strength of dhalalah as a direct textual indication.
5
Apply the limitation for hudud and qisas
Matters averted by doubts, such as hudud and qisas based on the hadith 'Avert hudud by doubts', cannot be proven by dhalalat al-nas because it does not provide the highest certainty.
This restriction preserves the principle of leniency in penal law.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سے زجر اور رکاوٹ ہو جائے ۔ لوگ قصاص کے خوف سے بنا۔ انسان کی توڑ پھوڑ سے باز آجائیں گے یہ توڑ پھوڑ تو فعل ہے. والزواجر اور تمام زواجر جیسے حدود و کفارات ہیں یہ تمام اجزہیتہ افعال ہیں ۔ ووجوب القصاص الخير جزا فعل ہونے کی یہ دوسری وجہ ہے . حاصل یہ کہ اگر ایک جماعت نے ایک انسان کو قتل کیا ہے تو اس جماعت قاتلین کلہم پر قصاص واجب ہو جائیگا تو معلوم ہوا کہ یہ جزا فعل ہے کیونکہ محل تو ایک ہے لیکن قصاص متعدد اشخاص پر ہے اس لئے کہ ان تمام کا فعلی حیثیت سے دخل ہے تو جتنا آدمیوں نے فعلاً اس قتل میں حصہ لیا ہے سب پر قصاص واجب ہے تو معلوم ہوا کہ یہ قصاص جنہ امہ فعل بھی ہے جیسے جزار محل ہے ۔ والثابت بدلالة النص كالثابت بالعبارة والاشارة يعني جو مسئلہ دلالتہ النص کے ساتھ ثابت ہو گا وہ برابر اور مساوی ہوگا فی الثبوت والقطعیہ اس مسئلہ کے ساتھ جو عبارۃ النص یا اشارہ النص کے ساتھ ثابت ہے الا عند التعارض مگر بوقت تعارض کے عبارۃ النص اور اشارۃ النص کو ترجیح حاصل ہو گی علی دلالۃ النص کیونکہ عبارة اور اشارة ثابت بالنظم وبالمعنى اللغوى ہیں اور دلالۃ النص ثابت بالمعنی ہے فقط اور اگر عبارۃ النص اور اشارۃ النص میں تعارض ہو جاتے تو پھر عبارۃ النص کو ترجیح ہوگی کیونکہ سوق کلام عبارة النص کے لئے موجب ترجیح ہے۔ وھو فوق القیاس اور دلالہ النص قیاس سے فائق ہے بلکہ خبر واحد پر بھی اسے فوقیت حاصل ہے لان المعنی فی القیاس کیونکہ معنی یعنی وہ علتہ جس کی وجہ سے قیاس کیا جاتا ہے اس کا ادراک من النص بالر ہی ہوتا ہے اور دلالہ النص اس کا ادراک لغتہ ہوتا ہے۔ فیثبت بہا ما یدرأ بالشبهات جو اشیاء مندرأ بالشبهات ہوتی ہیں یعنی حدود و قصاص جن کے متعلق رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا ہے ادرؤوا الحدود بالشبهات یہ اشیاء دلالۃ النص کے ساتھ ثابت نہیں ہو سکتی ۔ واعلم ان في بعض المسائل اور مسائل مذکورہ فی المتن میں اس بارے میں کلام ہے کہ یہ ثابت بدلالة النص ہیں یا ثابت بالقياس فعلیک بالتا عمل آپ غور و فکر کریں بہر حال وہ مصنف کے نزدیک دلالۃ النص کے ساتھ ثابت ہیں۔
From deterrence and obstruction. People, from fear of qisas, will stop from breaking and destroying. Breaking and destroying is an act. And all deterrents like hudud and kaffarat are all acts. And the obligation of qisas is the second reason for being a retributive act. In summary, if a group killed a person, then qisas becomes obligatory on all of that group of killers. So it is known that this retribution is an act because the locus is one but qisas is upon multiple persons because all of them have involvement in terms of act. So as many people as actually participated in the killing, all are obligated for qisas. So it is known that this qisas is also an act, like [؟]. And that which is proven by dhalalat al-nas is like that which is proven by ibarah and isharah; meaning a matter proven by dhalalat al-nas will be equal and equivalent in proof and definitiveness to a matter proven by ibarat al-nas or isharat al-nas, except when there is contradiction: then ibarat al-nas and isharat al-nas are given priority over dhalalat al-nas because ibarah and isharah are proven by the wording and the linguistic meaning, while dhalalat al-nas is proven only by the meaning. And if ibarat al-nas and isharat al-nas contradict each other, then ibarat al-nas is given priority because the flow of speech is a cause for priority for ibarat al-nas. And it is above qiyas; dhalalat al-nas is superior to qiyas, and even superior to khabar wahid because the meaning (the ‘illa) in qiyas is perceived from the text by inference, while dhalalat al-nas is perceived linguistically. By it are proven matters that are averted by doubts, i.e., matters that are averted by ambiguities, such as hudud and qisas, regarding which the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Avert the hudud by doubts.' These matters cannot be proven by dhalalat al-nas. And know that in some issues, there is discussion about whether they are proven by dhalalat al-nas or by qiyas; so you must reflect. Nevertheless, in the author’s view, they are proven by dhalalat al-nas.
Source pages p. 401

Commentary
This passage discusses the concept of dhalalat al-nas (indication of the text) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. It begins with a preceding example about qisas as a retributive act, showing that qisas is considered an act because it applies to multiple participants based on their actual involvement. Then it defines dhalalat al-nas: a ruling proven by dhalalat al-nas has the same weight in proof and definitiveness as one proven by ibarat al-nas (explicit wording) or isharat al-nas (implied meaning). However, if there is a conflict, ibarah and isharah take priority over dhalalah because they are established both by the wording and linguistic meaning, while dhalalah is only by meaning. If ibarah and isharah conflict, ibarah is prioritized due to the flow of speech. Dhalalah is superior to qiyas (analogy) and even khabar wahid (solitary report), because qiyas derives its ‘illa from the text by inference, while dhalalah derives it linguistically. However, matters that are averted by doubts (like hudud and qisas based on the hadith 'Avert hudud by doubts') cannot be proven by dhalalah. The author notes that some issues are debated whether they are proven by dhalalah or qiyas, but he holds they are proven by dhalalah.

Key Terms
دلالة النص (dhalalat al-nas): A ruling derived from the text through its understood meaning, not from explicit wording or implied indication.
عبارة النص (ibarat al-nas): The explicit wording of the text from which a ruling is directly derived.
اشارة النص (isharat al-nas): A ruling derived from the text through its implication, not the literal wording.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the default status of a ruling proven by dhalalat al-nas compared to one proven by ibarat al-nas?
A) It is weaker and only accepted if no other proof exists.
B) It is equal in proof and definitiveness, except when they contradict.
C) It is superior because it is based on linguistic meaning.
D) It is rejected in favor of qiyas.

Key Takeaway
Dhalalat al-nas is a robust textual indication equal to ibarah and isharah, yielding only at contradiction, and is superior to qiyas but cannot establish hudud or qisas.
